# Live Achievement Status

Last updated: 2026-05-26 (`.b.6.2.37.6` DONE — SV grammar LRM-extraction fix: `inside_expression` + `value_range` require LRM literal braces/brackets; uvm_pkg furthest 1,121,290 → 1,278,335 (+157K, ~14% more, ~42% through); release 1.0.130 (schema stays 3))

## Purpose
Provide a precise, always-current progress surface for the project using exactly four status levels:
- `Done`
- `Mostly Done`
- `In Progress`
- `Not Started`

This file is the authoritative live tracking view for "where we are now".

## Status Rules
- `Done`: the tracked claim is backed by a formally exhaustive, machine-checkable proof surface with no plausible coverage gap remaining for that claim.
- `Mostly Done`: the core implementation is landed and validated with strong executable evidence, but closure still depends on bounded follow-up work such as auto-derived exhaustiveness, stronger coverage proof, or removal of curated/manual proof gaps.
- `In Progress`: meaningful implementation has started, but core capabilities or validation are still missing.
- `Not Started`: no meaningful implementation has landed yet.

## Update Policy
- Review and update this file before every commit when a task changes actual project closure, remaining scope, or the next most important gap.
- When any live-status row changes, log that change here before commit and explicitly surface the changed snapshot in the user-facing completion message for that task.
- Even when no row changes, the commit-workflow completion message must still display the current live-status snapshot so task impact on the tracker stays visible.
- When a task does not change live status, say that status is unchanged rather than implying drift.
- Use only the four statuses above.
- Keep "Evidence" concrete and "Left To Close" explicit.
- Do not mark a row `Done` if its proof surface still depends on a curated/manual construct list where grammar-derived exhaustiveness is expected.
- Universal parser doctrine: any PGEN EBNF-based parser family is judged against the same professional-grade closure bar. Status differences across parser families reflect different amounts of landed proof, not different quality standards.

## Live Snapshot

Tracker note (2026-05-26): **`SV-EXH-PROOF.3.3.4.b.6.2.37.6` DONE — SV GRAMMAR LRM-EXTRACTION FIX: `inside_expression` + `value_range` require LRM literal braces/brackets; uvm_pkg furthest 1,121,290 → 1,278,335; release 1.0.129 → 1.0.130, schema STAYS 3 (`PGEN-SV-EXH-PROOF-0093`).** Two coordinated grammar rule edits per IEEE 1800 §A.8.3: (a) `value_range_sv_2017/2023` — the range alternative `( expression colon expression )?` (missing brackets, optional-empty fallthrough) → `lbrack expression colon expression rbrack` (LRM literal `[` and `]`); sv_2023 same fix across all 4 bracketed variants (range / dollar_lo / dollar_hi / tolerance). (b) `inside_expression_sv_2017/2023` — `kw_inside open_range_list*` (missing braces, zero-or-more fallthrough) → `kw_inside lbrace open_range_list rbrace` (LRM literal `{` and `}`). Surfaced by `.37.5`'s 1,121,290 furthest reaching `uvm_phase::jump`'s `phases.find(item) with (item.get_state() inside {[UVM_PHASE_STARTED:UVM_PHASE_CLEANUP]})` — the `inside {[1:5]}` LRM form requires BOTH the brace AND bracket literals. Pre-fix the broken rule shells (`?` / `*` quantifiers on the optional-empty bodies) made the parser silently "succeed" on empty matches without consuming the actual list, leaving the cursor stuck. Per the `.b.1`-precedent class of LRM-extraction-defect fixes (same pattern: read LRM literally; pgen extraction was missing the literal punctuators). **EMPIRICAL VERIFICATION:** 5-way inside-variant repro all PASS post-fix: `inside {1, 2}` (was PASS), `inside {[1:5]}` (was FAIL), `inside {[1:5], 10}` (was FAIL), `inside {[$:5]}` (was FAIL), `inside {[1:$]}` (was FAIL). Lib (--features generated_parsers) **609/609 PASS**; lib (no-features) **548/548 PASS**; clippy ✅; SV external corpus triage gate **10 PASS / 4 FAIL / 0 TIMEOUT** — binary stable; **uvm_pkg ×{2017,2023} furthest_position 1,121,290 → 1,278,335** (+157,045 bytes deeper, ~14% more; reaches ~1.28M of ~3.0M preprocessed bytes = ~42% through uvm_pkg). uvm_compat_pkg ×{2017,2023} unchanged at 116752 (H1 territory). **uvm_pkg furthest_position arc continues:** Slice-54 baseline 19378 → pre-`.35.1` 113637 → `.35.1` 162162 → `.36.4` 181413 → `.37.2` 828954 → `.37.3` 866292 → `.37.5` 1,121,290 → **`.37.6` 1,278,335** = ~66× deeper than Slice-54's baseline; ~11.5× deeper than `.35.1`. NO-WORKAROUNDS HIERARCHY: **level 1** — pure grammar LRM alignment; no new annotation, no engine change. Strictly-more-permissive (SVPP-0002/REGEX-0083): previously-unparseable range-inside-inside now parses; previously-PASSING `inside {1, 2}` still parses via the same path through the new literal braces. Per the new push-pacing rule (user 2026-05-26): unpushed accumulation = 2 commits (Slice-81 + Slice-82); not pushing yet. Frontier: `.b.6.2.37.7+` (next defect past uvm_pkg byte ~1.28M) OR `.b.6.2.35.{2..16}` ungated-rule remediation OR H1 (uvm_compat_pkg — depends on uvm_pkg PASSing first).

Tracker note (2026-05-26): **`SV-EXH-PROOF.3.3.4.b.6.2.37.5` DONE — SV GRAMMAR FIX: `context_member_method_call` member-loop accepts indexed members; uvm_pkg furthest 866292 → 1,121,290 (+255K deeper); release 1.0.128 → 1.0.129, schema STAYS 3 (`PGEN-SV-EXH-PROOF-0092`).** One-token grammar edit at `grammars/systemverilog.ebnf:2880`: `( dot identifier &dot )+` → `( dot identifier constant_bit_select &dot )+`. Surfaced by `.37.3`'s 866292 furthest_position reaching uvm_pkg's `uvm_report_message_element_container::do_copy` foreach body: `elements.push_back(urme_container.elements[i].clone())` — the argument `c.elements[i].clone()` is a 3-level chain `instance . indexed_member . method_call`. Pre-fix the `.b.6.2`-era `context_member_method_call` rule (for identifier-rooted 3+level chains) only accepted bare identifiers between dots; with a `[bit_select]` between identifiers the `&dot` lookahead failed (`[` ≠ `.`) and the rule was rejected. Fix: add `constant_bit_select` (which is `( lbrack constant_expression rbrack )*` matching zero-or-more `[...]`, so matches empty when no index is present) between the member identifier and the `&dot` lookahead — `dot identifier [i] &dot` now parses. **EMPIRICAL VERIFICATION:** 6-way minimal repro all PASS post-fix: `c.elements.clone()` (no index, was PASS), `c.elements[i].clone()` (variable index, was FAIL), `c.elements[0].clone()` (literal index, was FAIL), `c.a.b.c.method()` (4-segment no index, was PASS), `c.a.b[i].c.method()` (5-segment middle index, was FAIL), `c.a[i].b.method()` (4-segment head-of-member index, was FAIL). Lib (--features generated_parsers) **609/609 PASS**; lib (no-features) **548/548 PASS**; clippy ✅; SV external corpus triage gate **10 PASS / 4 FAIL / 0 TIMEOUT** — binary count stable; **uvm_pkg ×{2017,2023} furthest_position 866292 → 1,121,290** (+254,998 bytes deeper, ~30% more; reaches ~1.12M of ~3.0M preprocessed bytes = ~37% of the way through uvm_pkg). uvm_compat_pkg ×{2017,2023} unchanged at 116752 (H1 territory). **uvm_pkg furthest_position arc continues:** Slice-54 baseline 19378 → pre-`.35.1` 113637 → `.35.1` 162162 → `.36.4` 181413 → `.37.2` 828954 → `.37.3` 866292 → **`.37.5` 1,121,290** = ~58× deeper than Slice-54's baseline; ~10× deeper than `.35.1`. NO-WORKAROUNDS HIERARCHY: **level 1** — existing grammar primitive (`constant_bit_select` is widely used in the SV grammar; this slice just lifts it into the chain member-loop). Per [[feedback_grammar_rules_must_consult_store]] the rule remains gated by `@predicate has_fact(variable_binding, $head)`. Backwards-compatible: when no `[...]` is present, `constant_bit_select` matches empty, so `a.b.c.method()` parses byte-identically to pre-fix (existing shape `{head, members, method, chain}` preserved). Strictly-more-permissive: previously-unparseable `a.b[i].c.method()` now parses with the SAME shape (just with the indexed member captured in the members list). SVPP-0002/REGEX-0083 category. Frontier: `.b.6.2.37.6+` (next defect surfaced past uvm_pkg line ~32K) OR `.b.6.2.35.{2..16}` Table-B/C/D ungated-rule remediation OR H1 (uvm_compat_pkg — still depends on uvm_pkg PASSing first). Books↔code same-commit lockstep (grammar + SV contract 1.0.129 + SV book changelog-index + schema-versioning + CHANGES + this note + DEVELOPMENT_NOTES + TASK_TREE + SV-EXH-PROOF leaves + MEMORY). Per the new push-pacing rule (user 2026-05-26): commit per slice, push at ~30 unpushed OR explicit "push now". This slice does NOT auto-push.

Tracker note (2026-05-26): **`SV-EXH-PROOF.3.3.4.b.6.2.37.3` DONE — SV GRAMMAR FIX: `Class::member` as primary expression + lvalue; bundled release 1.0.127 → 1.0.128 covering `.36.4 + .36.5 + .37.0 + .37.1 + .37.2 + .37.3` (`PGEN-SV-EXH-PROOF-0090`).** Three coordinated rule edits in `grammars/systemverilog.ebnf`: `primary_hier_scope_prefix` + `variable_lvalue_scope` + `nonrange_variable_lvalue` all gain a `class_scope` alternative. Surfaced by `.37.2`'s 4.5× deepening — at uvm_pkg line 25726 inside `uvm_callbacks #(T, CB)`, `super_t::m_typename = tname;` (typedef-aliased parameterized base, scoped-member assignment) was unparseable. Pre-fix the grammar accepted ONLY `local::` (`kw_class_qualifier`) and `pkg::` (`non_typedef_package_scope`) as primary/lvalue scope prefixes; `Class::` was missing — pre-existing pgen grammar defect surfaced by H2's depth advance. Per IEEE 1800 §A.8.4 the LRM's `primary` accepts a `class_qualifier` prefix and the LRM's `class_qualifier ::= [ local:: ] [ implicit_class_handle . | class_scope ]` — the `class_scope` arm was missing from pgen's primary/lvalue scope prefixes. The `class_scope` branch is gated by `known_unscoped_class_scope_class_identifier`'s `fact_attribute_equals(type_name, $body, declaration_family, class)` predicate, so it fires only for known class names (no risk of false positives on package or ambiguous identifiers). **EMPIRICAL VERIFICATION:** 4-way minimal repro all PASS post-fix (all FAILed pre-fix): `super_t::m_name = "x"` (LVALUE typedef alias), `base#(T)::m_name = "x"` (LVALUE direct parameterized), `string x = super_t::m_name` (RVALUE), `return super_t::m_name` (RVALUE in return). Lib (--features generated_parsers) **609/609 PASS**; lib (no-features) **548/548 PASS**; clippy ✅; SV external corpus triage gate **10 PASS / 4 FAIL / 0 TIMEOUT** — binary count stable; **uvm_pkg ×{2017,2023} furthest_position 828954 → 866292** (+37,338 bytes deeper; reaches past the parameterized-class chain). uvm_compat_pkg unchanged at 116752 (H1 territory). **BUNDLED RELEASE 1.0.127 → 1.0.128** — six slices' release-bump candidates (each individually deferred) all land together: (a) `.36.4` engine memoization-delta replay, (b) `.36.5` bootstrap `**` → FlattenSpread, (c-e) `.37.0/.37.1/.37.2` H2 SV-stdlib auto-load, (f) `.37.3` `Class::member` grammar fix. Schema STAYS 3 (no AST shape vocabulary change throughout). All slices SVPP-0002/REGEX-0083 strictly-more-permissive category (previously-unparseable inputs now parse; previously-parseable byte-identical). Tracker note (2026-05-26): **`SV-EXH-PROOF.3.3.4.b.6.2.37.2` DONE — H2 ENGINE+ADAPTER FIX LANDED: SV stdlib auto-load is wired end-to-end; uvm_pkg furthest_position 181413 → 828954 (+647K bytes, ~4.5× deeper; reaches the next LRM defect layer at `uvm_visitor#(uvm_component)` parameterized-class chain). H2 is verified as a corpus-DEEPENER — necessary not sufficient, same onion-peeling pattern as `.b.1`'s conditional_statement fix (`PGEN-SV-EXH-PROOF-0089`).** Two coordinated changes: (a) **codegen change** in `rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs::generate_parse_method` — `parse()` now snapshots `semantic_runtime_state.facts()` BEFORE the reset-to-fresh-state and re-pushes them after, preserving preloads across the reset. Root cause traced via `--trace` on `data_type`: the reset (originally for clearing leftovers between parses) was wiping the preloaded std-package facts before any rule fired, so `has_fact(type_name, process)` consistently returned false despite the preload. (b) **SV adapter wiring** in `rust/src/parser_registry.rs` — new `preload_systemverilog_stdlib` helper that reads `<repo>/parser_libs/sv_<profile>_std/package/std.facts.json` and pushes facts into `semantic_runtime_state` via `push_fact_record` BEFORE `parse_full_systemverilog_file`. Wired into all 4 SV parser-construction sites (`parse_with_systemverilog_profile`, `parse_with_systemverilog_detail_profile`, `parse_with_systemverilog_detail_profile_with_library`, `parse_with_systemverilog_ast_json_profile`). Tracker note (2026-05-25): **`SV-EXH-PROOF.3.3.4.b.6.2.36.5` DONE — LATENT REGRESSION FIX (PGEN-RGX-0077): bootstrap parser peeks `**` FIRST in BOTH `unified_return_ast.rs::parse_postfix_chain` (scalar `$N**`) AND `parse_array` (array-wrapped `[$N**]`), producing `FlattenSpread(base)` instead of `Spread(Spread(base))` (`PGEN-SV-EXH-PROOF-0086`).** Tools-first diagnosis (per [[feedback_tools_first_no_guessing]]) initially routed to `parse_postfix_chain`; a follow-up `[$1**]` regression test exposed that the array-context codepath (`parse_array`) has its OWN special-case `ends_with('*')` handler that stripped one `*` and re-parsed via `parse_value`, also producing `Spread(Spread)` silently — both paths needed the same `**`-before-`*` fix. The downstream codegen (intact in source: `ast_return_transform.rs::generate_array_transform`'s FlattenSpread arm peels `Alternative` + spreads `Json(Array)`) was unreachable for `[$1**]` because the AST never carried `FlattenSpread`. The bug had been masked since pre-slice-66 by stale `regex_parser.rs` (last regen May 22); `.36.4`'s full regen exposed the regression. Per user direction "task-tree track it to debug and fix it later. Just fix the currently observed issue." this slice fixes it surgically. Both bootstrap codepaths now agree with the EBNF surface (`return_annotation.ebnf` orders `flat_spread_expression` BEFORE `spread_expression` per PEG ordered choice). One existing unit test (`test_parse_extraction_operators` — `$2::1**`) had encoded the BUG'S shape — corrected to assert the right one-level `FlattenSpread(QuantifiedExtraction)` form; one NEW regression test (`[$1**]` → `Array { FlattenSpread(PositionalRef(1)) }`) pins the array-context bootstrap shape. THE PRACTICAL FIX (the one that flipped `regex_0077` test from FAIL to PASS) actually came via `make focus_regex` rebuilding ast_pipeline with `--features generated_parsers` (the codegen then takes the GENERATED return_annotation parser path that produces correct typed FlattenSpread JSON via `parse_typed_return_value`); my bootstrap fix is the defense-in-depth secondary surface for `--bootstrap-mode` builds. Both surfaces now agree. **EMPIRICAL VERIFICATION:** PGEN-RGX-0077 test PASS (was FAIL since pre-slice-66); `\Qab*\E{2,}` AST shows `pattern[0][0]` as 4 flat piece objects not nested; regex_parser.rs now emits 4× `flatten_spread_element` strings (was 0); lib (--features generated_parsers) **609/609 PASS** (was 608/609 at `.36.4`); lib (no-features) **548/548 PASS**; SV external corpus triage gate **10 PASS / 4 FAIL / 0 TIMEOUT** — stable at 10/14 (residual 4 = uvm_pkg ×{2017,2023} + uvm_compat_pkg ×{2017,2023}); clippy ✅. NO-WORKAROUNDS HIERARCHY: this is **level 5** equivalent — a parser-agnostic bootstrap-parser fix that brings the bootstrap into ordered-choice agreement with the EBNF surface (mandatory for both generator surfaces to produce identical AST for the same annotation). RELEASE FRAMING: bundled with `.36.6`'s combined release decision for `.36.4 + .36.5` (engine extension + bootstrap fix; no AST shape change → release-bump-only candidate, schema stays 3). Tracker note (2026-05-25): **`SV-EXH-PROOF.3.3.4.b.6.2.36.4` DONE — ENGINE FIX: memoization-delta replay closes the memoization × semantic-store composition gap pinned by `.36.3` (`PGEN-SV-EXH-PROOF-0085`).** Parser-agnostic engine extension. `MemoEntry` gains a `semantic_delta: Option<SemanticRuntimeDelta>` field; `memoized_call` captures the delta at body-execution time and REPLAYS it on every cache hit. For grammars without semantic annotations (regex / json / ebnf), the delta is always empty so replay is a no-op (zero perf cost). For grammars with semantic annotations (SV / VHDL / RTL), the delta is typically O(few) per rule, so replay cost is bounded. **EMPIRICAL VERIFICATION:** class_param_t.sv (`class c #(type T=int); function void f(T value); endfunction endclass`) NOW PASSES (was FAIL at byte 42); uvm_bvu_minimal.sv (uvm_bit_vector_utils#(type T=int) shape with `static function string to_string(T value, int size); endfunction`) NOW PASSES (was FAIL at byte 100); iso5/iso4 + iso1/2/3/6 + simple_typedef + 4 sanity controls all unchanged behavior. Tracker note (2026-05-25): **`SV-EXH-PROOF.3.3.4.b.6.2.36.3` DONE — investigation using `.36.2`'s tool pinned the TRUE ROOT CAUSE: memoization caches parse results but NOT semantic-runtime side effects (`PGEN-SV-EXH-PROOF-0084`).** Bundled instrumentation extension (codegen-level fast-path now also pushes/pops the rule_context_stack, closing a chain-trace gap in `.36.2`). The class_param_t.sv minimal repro fails because: `type_assignment` is first called inside parameter_port_list's branch 1 (which emits T then fails), memoization caches the AST result without the semantic delta, branch 3 calls type_assignment at the same position → MEMO HIT returns cached AST without re-firing emit_fact → T never reaches the committed state → class body's `has_fact(T) → false` → function arg parse fails. This is a fundamental interaction between memoization and the semantic store: memo cache stores AST + end_pos + raw_semantic_content but NOT the emit_fact/scope-change side effects. C3-A/C3-B's transactional state management doesn't compose with memoization. THIS DOES NOT VINDICATE THE RETIRED PERSISTENCE MANDATE — that retirement was for the iso5/iso4 / port-list defect (structural, ungated rule); the memoization-delta interaction is a separately-discovered class. Fix routed to `.b.6.2.36.4`: extend MemoEntry with a SemanticRuntimeDelta field, capture at memo write, replay at memo hit. Initial scope: fact replay; scope replay is a separate consideration. VERIFIED: lib (no-features) 548/548 PASS post-regen; iso5/iso4 + 4 controls + corpus 10/14 preserved (pure instrumentation extension, no behavior change). NO release/contract bump. This slice is the canonical exemplar of [[feedback_why_and_where_before_solution]] — the tool from `.36.2`, refined here, made a previously-mysterious bug surgically diagnosable in one focused trace.

Tracker note (2026-05-21): **`SV-EXH-PROOF.3.3.4.b.3` DONE — PARSER-AGNOSTIC ENGINE LAYER 0: unified quantifier engine; uniform per-iteration atomicity across `?` / `*` / `+` / `{N}` / `{N,M}` / `{N,}` / `{,M}`; release 1.0.126 (schema stays 3); SV external corpus stays 8/14 — Layer 0 is INFRASTRUCTURE; regex broader corpus / RGX conformance ✅ 44/0 unaffected (proves the unified codegen is behavior-equivalent across the entire conformance suite) (`PGEN-SV-EXH-PROOF-0029`).** User strategic line (2026-05-21): "After Layer 0, all the repetition in the EBNF shall have the right behavior." Prior codegen in `rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs::generate_quantified_logic` (and `ast_code_generator.rs::generate_quantified_content`) special-cased exactly three operators (`*`, `+`, `?`) in three independently-written code paths, with an asymmetric defect — the FIRST iteration of `+` was emitted INLINE without `try_parse` wrapping. Bounded forms (`{N}` / `{N,M}` / `{N,}` / `{,M}`) declared in `grammars/ebnf.ebnf:149-189` were never implemented (the `_ => Err("Unknown quantifier")` fallthrough). **Fix:** new `parse_quantifier_bounds(quantifier: &str) -> Option<(usize, Option<usize>)>` helper in `rust/src/ast_pipeline/mod.rs` maps every surface form to `(min, max)` (4 unit tests cover happy path + whitespace + invalid forms incl. `{5,2}` rejected). Both codegen functions rewritten as ONE `loop` with EVERY iteration wrapped in `try_parse` (per-iteration atomicity is uniform). When `min > 0`, codegen emits `let quantifier_start_position = parser.position;` before the loop and restores `parser.position = quantifier_start_position;` on min-failure before `Err(Backtrack)` — quantifier-level atomicity (the user's stated `{N}` semantics: "the cursor is left at the position it had before trying to match `<group>{N}`"). For `min == 0` (`*` / `?`) the bind + check are elided to avoid always-false comparisons + 495 unused-variable warnings. Max-count (`{N}` / `{N,M}` / `{,M}`) emits `if iteration_count >= #m_lit { break; }`. Zero-length guard + SAFETY_LIMIT (10_000) preserved. **Release bump, NO schema bump** — `?` / `*` / `+` BEHAVIOR-EQUIVALENT on success; BEHAVIOR-EQUIVALENT-OR-MORE-CORRECT on failure (prior `+` first-iter inline path could leak partial cursor; unified path rolls back at the quantifier boundary). Bounded forms unparseable pre-fix; Layer 0 makes them parser-agnostic infrastructure (no current grammar uses them); SVPP-0002/REGEX-0083 strictly-more-permissive category. USER SEMANTICS, CONFIRMED IMPLEMENTED: per-iter cursor save+restore (handled by `try_parse`) + quantifier-level atomicity for `min > 0` (handled by `quantifier_start_position`). VERIFIED: lib **465/465** PASS no-features (+4 `parse_quantifier_bounds` unit tests); SV smoke (`module m; endmodule` / `if (1) $display("ok");` / else-if chain / for-loop) PASS via fresh release `parseability_probe`; SV shape-contract GREEN. **RGX broader corpus / conformance 44/0 ✅** via `cargo run --features generated_parsers --release --bin test_runner -- --parser regex` after `make focus_regex` regen — proves the unified codegen produces a regex parser with identical behavior across the entire conformance suite. **SV external corpus `8/14 → 10/14`** (fresh triage gate 2026-05-21 09:55) — `friscv_rv32i_core ×{2017,2023}` now PASS. HONEST ROOT-CAUSE UPDATE: I had hypothesised Layer 0 was pure infrastructure with no corpus delta expected; the gate proved that wrong by +2 cases. The friscv_rv32i blocker was NOT a separate statement-level grammar defect (the prior `.3.3.6` categorization); it was the prior codegen's asymmetric `+`-first-iter-not-wrapped-in-`try_parse` defect. Layer 0 wraps the first iter of `+` uniformly with every other iter — the cursor rolls back cleanly on first-iter failure — and friscv_rv32i parses end-to-end. The BEHAVIORAL DIFFERENCE on the prior `+` first-iter-FAILURE path was real (not behavior-equivalent as I had claimed at design time). Tracker note (2026-05-20): **`SV-EXH-PROOF.3.3.3` DONE — FIRST DELIBERATE ENGINE FIX (parser-agnostic, in the generator) + SV grammar wrapper composite; classic Rust `?`-bypasses-cleanup bug in `with_semantic_runtime_rule_transaction` (SEMTRACE-pinned after 3 prior hypotheses disproven); release 1.0.121, AST-dump schema stays `3`; minimal repro `my_t [3:0] x` PASSES (was unfixable); regex broader corpus / RGX conformance ✅ 44/0 unaffected; external-corpus stays `6/14` (foundation engine fix — `.3.3.4` cross-package import is the corpus mover) (`PGEN-SV-EXH-PROOF-0024`).** Root cause (SEMTRACE-definitive across 1664 trace lines): `with_semantic_runtime_rule_transaction` (`rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs`) `std::mem::take`-s `self.semantic_runtime_state` (leaving `Default==new()` valid-but-EMPTY), then performs `?`-fallible calls (`f(self)?`, `apply_*?`, `resolve_predicate?`); a `?` early-return propagated out of the ENTIRE function, JUMPING OVER the trailing `if result.is_err() { restore original }` — leaving self.state EMPTY, silently destroying every fact emitted by prior COMMITTED sibling rules. Decisive evidence: `RESTORE` fired **0×** / `took post-body state (self.state→EMPTY)` **9×** / fact-flow `declared_type_identifier facts(1)=[type_name=my_t] EXIT OK → … → use-site facts(0)=[] never restored`. **Fix (engine, parser-agnostic, IIFE/"try-block" emulation)**: wrap the fallible body in `(|| -> ParseResult<…> {…})()` so every `?` returns into `result`, making the restore reachable on every non-commit exit. Zero `unsafe`; zero behaviour change on success; benefits every generated parser. RAII Drop-guard considered (panic-safe by strict def.) but rejected: not cleanly safe-Rust here (post-take body calls `&self` methods, guard would conflict; only `*mut`+`unsafe` works); deferred since `Default==new()` makes IIFE panic-ROBUST (parser never `catch_unwind`s mid-parse). **Fix (SV grammar composite)**: `checked_type_identifier := type_identifier -> {body:$1.body}` + `@predicate has_fact args:[type_name,$body]`, routing `known_unscoped_block/data_type_identifier` through it (proven `.3.3.1`/`.3.3.2` idiom). **Release bump 1.0.120→1.0.121, schema STAYS 3** (strictly-more-permissive; affected declarations were silently unparseable, no such AST ever emitted; SVPP-0002/REGEX-0083 category). VERIFIED: minimal repro PASSES; SEMTRACE confirmed RESTORE fires 110× (was 0); use-site `has_fact[type_name,my_t]` resolves+TRUE; class/typedef/let/`#(parameter…)`/localparam/builtin-dim no-regression (memo ON, normal). Inventory **2297→2299** (+2: new wrapper). SV shape-contract GREEN. **regex broader corpus / RGX conformance ✅ 44/0** (critical downstream unaffected). external-corpus **stays `6/14`** — `.3.3.3` is the FOUNDATION engine fix (the `?`-bypass state-leak was masking every downstream semantic-fact-based fix); residual 8 cases blocked by DISTINCT defects → **`.3.3.4` cross-package `import pkg::*` type-name visibility (the actual corpus mover, ~6 cases — veer ×2 + uvm ×2 + uvm_compat ×2)** + `.3.3.6` (statement-level, friscv_rv32i ×2). Pre-existing `auto_gate_regex/rtl_const_expr_inventory_wide_shape` failures (decisively confirmed pre-existing at `.3.3.2` via git-stash baseline check) tracked as `.3.3.5`. Strategic line (user 2026-05-20): EBNF + the AST-pipeline engine must acquire all the parser-agnostic features needed to cleanly and elegantly parse the whole external SV corpus; `.3.3.3` IIFE is the first such parser-agnostic engine feature; `.3.3.4` will follow the same lens. Tracker note (2026-05-18): **`PGEN-RGX-0085` FIXED — regex parenthesis-nesting ceiling (no more host SIGABRT); tree `RGX-0085` CLOSED (`PGEN-RGX-0085-0001`).** User-directed priority interrupt (ordered `PGEN-RGX-0085` then `PGEN-RGX-0086`, before resuming `SV-EXH-PROOF.3.1`; "be extremely careful"). Tracker note (2026-05-18): **`PGEN-RGX-0087` FULLY RESOLVED & CLOSED — FIX2.3 closed the last residual (octal `>\377` overflow); regex release 1.1.80 / contract 1.1.82 (`PGEN-RGX-0087-FIX2-0003`).** The remaining `PGEN-RGX-0087` piece: PGEN's bare `\ddd` octal payload `/([0-7]{1,3})/` had no PCRE2 octal-range check, so `\6666666666` (testinput9:287 `(?i:A{1,}\6666666666)`), `\400`, `\666`, `\777`, `\7777` and the class forms `[\666]`/`[\400]` were ACCEPTed where PCRE2 10.47 **hard-errors** (err 151, octal `>\377` 8-bit non-UTF — in **both** pattern-body and `[...]` class context; PCRE2 does not truncate a `>0o377` triple). Grammar-only fix (two coordinated edits, executed from the `PGEN-RGX-0087-FIX2-0002` pinned design): (A) split `octal_escape_short_payload` — a 3-octal-digit run valid only if `[0-3]`-led (≤0o377), a 1-2-digit run only if octal-COMPLETE (proven `!"0"…!"7"` lookahead idiom, `-> $1` per branch ⇒ `octal_escape`'s `digits:$1` unchanged; overflow triple matches neither ⇒ `octal_escape` fails ⇒ reject); (B) FIX2.1's `class_simple_escape` gains `!"0"…!"7"` octal-digit guards (NOT 8/9) so an octal-overflow `\<octal-digit>` is not class-shorthand-rescued while `\8`/`\9` stay (FIX2.1 preserved). **Decisive empirical `--parse-dump-ast-pretty` byte-identical proof** (pre vs post): the entire RGX-0084 octal family + `\10`@9g/`\199`@0g/`(a)\12`/`\3777`/`\377`/`\012`/`\07`/`\0`/`\00`/`\000`/`\77`/`\7`-backref + FIX2.1 `[\8]`/`[\9]`/`[\88]`/`[\377]`/`[\012]`/`[\0]` + RGX-0087 `\81`@8g — ALL byte-identical; only the previously-wrongly-accepted overflow set now REJECTs; `\3777`→octal"377"+lit"7". Tracker note (2026-05-03): **regex.ebnf slice 40 of N — `modifier_item` per-branch typed (closes `inline_modifiers.spec` end-to-end).** Twelfth sub-rule typing slice. modifier_item split from 3 branches with internal optionals into 5 explicit branches: `"a" restrict -> {char:"a", restrict:$2}` / `"a" -> "a"` / `"xx" -> "xx"` / `"x" -> "x"` / `modifier_char` passthrough. Eliminates the `[]` interleaving from slice 39's set/unset arrays. Empirical: `(?ix)` → `set:["i", "x"]` (was `["i", "x", []]`); `(?aDx)` → `set:[{char:"a", restrict:"D"}, "x"]` (mixed string + object); `(?xx)` → `set:["xx"]` (matched doubled-x branch). **`inline_modifiers.spec` and `scoped_inline_modifiers.spec` now end-to-end typed across 4 sub-rule levels** (slices 24+31+39+40). A complete `(?aDx-m)` surfaces as `{type:"atom", kind:"inline_modifiers", spec:{reset:false, seq:{set:[{char:"a", restrict:"D"}, "x"], unset:["m"]}}}`. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.69` → `1.1.70`; contract `1.1.71` → `1.1.72`. New "Release 1.1.70 / Contract 1.1.72" section in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md). Regex AST schema version stays `1`. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers --features ebnf_dual_run` 495 / 0. Manifest gets 4 new entries. `make regex_parser_book_gate` green.

Tracker note (2026-05-03): **regex.ebnf slice 39 of N — `modifier_seq` + `modifier_group` typed (`{set, unset}` shape).** Eleventh sub-rule typing slice. 4 grammar changes: modifier_seq split from 2 branches (with parens-grouped optional pair) into 3 explicit branches; modifier_group `[$1**]` flatten-spread. Empirical: `(?i)` → `seq:{set:["i"], unset:[]}`; `(?ix-m)` → `seq:{set:["i", "x", []], unset:["m"]}`; `(?-i)` → `seq:{set:[], unset:["i"]}`. Same parens-grouped-optional-pair workaround pattern as slice 37 (version_number) — split into N explicit branches. Set/unset arrays may have interleaved `[]` markers for optional-sub-element items (e.g. `(?ix)` → `set:["i", "x", []]` where the trailing `[]` is the un-matched `"x"?` slot inside the `"x" "x"?` modifier_item branch). Per-rule typing of `modifier_item` (would clean the interleaving) deferred to a separate slice. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.68` → `1.1.69`; contract `1.1.70` → `1.1.71`. New "Release 1.1.69 / Contract 1.1.71" section in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md). Regex AST schema version stays `1`. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers --features ebnf_dual_run` 495 / 0. Manifest gets 4 new entries. `make regex_parser_book_gate` green.

Tracker note (2026-05-03): **PGEN-RGX-0080 logged (queued behind return-annotations campaign; fix order updated to 0080 → 0079 → 0078).** Counted quantifier `{m,n}` rejects whitespace next to the comma. PCRE2 default mode accepts whitespace anywhere inside `{...}`. Same misparse class as PGEN-RGX-0006 / PGEN-RGX-0079. Logged in `docs/contracts/PGEN_RELEASED_PARSER_BUG_LEDGER.md` as `REGEX-0080`.

Tracker note (2026-05-03): **regex.ebnf slice 38 of N — `returned_capture_subroutine` outer typed.** Tenth sub-rule typing slice. 1 annotation: `returned_capture_subroutine -> {subroutine:$1, captures:$2}`. Empirical: `(?&name(1))` → `target:{subroutine:{kind:"named", name:"name"}, captures:["(", {sign:[], value:1}, [], ")"]}`. **Field-naming decision:** inner field is `subroutine` (not `target`) to avoid `target.target.kind` collision with the outer `subroutine_call.target`. Consumer reads `obj.target.subroutine.kind` cleanly. **`captures` still raw** — `returned_capture_group_list` parens-grouped repetition can't currently be flattened via the annotation language (no positional indexing into matched pairs); grammar restructuring to recursive pair form (`group "," tail | group` with `[$1, $3**]`) OR annotation-language extension (`$3**.field`) would fix — saved for follow-up slice. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.67` → `1.1.68`; contract `1.1.69` → `1.1.70`. New "Release 1.1.68 / Contract 1.1.70" section in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md). Regex AST schema version stays `1`. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers --features ebnf_dual_run` 495 / 0. Manifest gets 1 new entry. `make regex_parser_book_gate` green.

Tracker note (2026-05-03): **regex.ebnf slice 37 of N — `version_number` `{major, minor}` typed.** Ninth sub-rule typing slice. `version_number` split into 2 explicit branches (instead of `digits ("." digits)?` parens-grouped form) for clean `{major:int, minor:int|null}` typed shape. Same accept set; PEG tries longer form first. Empirical: `(?(VERSION>=10.0)foo)` → `number:{major:10, minor:0}`; `(?(VERSION>=11)foo)` → `number:{major:11, minor:null}`; `(?(VERSION=10.40)foo)` → `number:{major:10, minor:40}`. **`version_condition` end-to-end typed** — combined with slice 32's outer typing, full pattern surfaces as `condition:{kind:"version", operator:">=", number:{major:10, minor:0}}`. Annotation language doesn't currently support extracting from parens-grouped optional pairs via positional/field access; the 2-branch split is the simplest typed shape with `null` (not `[]`) for absent-minor case. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.66` → `1.1.67`; contract `1.1.68` → `1.1.69`. New "Release 1.1.67 / Contract 1.1.69" section in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md). Tracker note (2026-05-03): **regex.ebnf slice 36 of N — condition_assertion / alpha_condition_assertion / condition_callout_assertion / condition_callout typed (closes condition Or-of-9 fully).** Eighth sub-rule typing slice. 7 annotations across 4 condition-context rules. `condition_assertion` per-branch `-> {kind:"lookahead"|"lookbehind", positive, body}` + alpha-passthrough. `alpha_condition_assertion -> {kind:"alpha_lookaround", name, body}`. `condition_callout -> {kind:"callout", arg}`. `condition_callout_assertion -> {kind:"callout_assertion", callout, assertion}`. Empirical: `(?(?=foo)yes)` → `condition:{kind:"lookahead", positive:true, body:<pattern>}`; `(?(?<!qux)yes)` → `condition:{kind:"lookbehind", positive:false}`; `(?(*pla:foo)yes)` → `condition:{kind:"alpha_lookaround", name:"pla"}`. **Intentional `kind` collision with slice 23's atom-level lookaround typing** — distinguishing field is `type:"atom"` (atom-level only). **`condition` Or-of-9 status: 7 of 9 typed** (`define`, `version`, `recursion` ×2, `condition_callout_assertion`, `condition_assertion` ×4 + alpha, `alpha_condition_assertion`); 2 untyped intentionally (`name_ref` and `name` — reused outside condition context); 2 pre-typed (`signed_digits`, `digits`). **`conditional` end-to-end typed.** **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.65` → `1.1.66`; contract `1.1.67` → `1.1.68`. New "Release 1.1.66 / Contract 1.1.68" section in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md). Tracker note (2026-05-02): **regex.ebnf slice 23 of N — lookaround family typed (7 sub-rules).** Largest slice yet — 7 annotations across 7 lookaround sub-rules in one batch. `lookahead_pos`/`lookahead_neg` collapse to `kind:"lookahead"` with `positive` boolean (`true`/`false`); same for `lookbehind`. Non-atomic forms get distinct kinds (`kind:"non_atomic_lookahead"`/`kind:"non_atomic_lookbehind"`) since PCRE2 only supports positive variants; `positive:true` field is included for uniform consumer code. Alpha-form `(*<name>:...)` carries the alpha_lookaround_name in `name` field. Empirical: `(?=foo)` → `{type:"atom", kind:"lookahead", positive:true, body:<pattern>}`; `(?!bar)` → `positive:false`; `(?<=baz)`/`(?<!qux)` → `kind:"lookbehind"`; `(?*alpha)`/`(?<*beta)` → `non_atomic_*`; `(*pla:gamma)` → `kind:"alpha_lookaround", name:"pla"`; `(*nla:delta)` → `name:"nla"`. **Lookaround family typed end-to-end.** Three patterns combined: 2-syntactic-form collapse via `positive`/`negated` boolean (slice 17/21 convention); distinct kind for non-atomic (PCRE2 only has positive variants); alpha-form `name` field for opener-name dispatch. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.52` → `1.1.53`; contract `1.1.54` → `1.1.55`. New "Release 1.1.53 / Contract 1.1.55" section in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md). Regex AST schema version stays `1`. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers --features ebnf_dual_run` 495 / 0. Tracker note (2026-05-02): **regex.ebnf slice 20 of N — `comment_group` typed.** `comment_group = "(?#" comment_text ")" -> {type:"atom", kind:"comment", text:$2}`. `comment_text` rewritten from `comment_char*` chain to regex literal `/([^)]*)/`. The `?` after `comment_text` in `comment_group` body was dropped — the regex literal accepts empty match, making the optional marker redundant. Empirical: `(?#hello)` → `{type:"atom", kind:"comment", text:"hello"}`; `(?#)` → `{text:""}`; `(?#multi word comment)` → `{text:"multi word comment"}`; `(?#with [special] chars)` → `{text:"with [special] chars"}`. **`text` is always a string**, including the empty case (real `""`, not `[]`). Char-set coverage: `[^)]*` matches the previous `comment_char*` chain semantics (any char except `)`). Continues the multi-char-chain → regex-literal pattern from slices 11 (`name`) / 15 (`hex_digits`) / 16 (`octal_digits`) / 17 (`prop_name`). **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.49` → `1.1.50`; contract `1.1.51` → `1.1.52`. Tracker note (2026-05-02): **regex.ebnf slice 18 of N — `quoted_literal` typed.** First atom-subtree slice after the escape closure. `quoted_literal = "\\Q" quoted_literal_char* "\\E" -> {type:"atom", kind:"quoted_literal", body:$2}`. Empirical: `\Qhello\E` → `{type:"atom", kind:"quoted_literal", body:["h","e","l","l","o"]}` (was `["\\Q", [<chars>], "\\E"]`); `\Q\E` → `{body:[]}`; `\Qabc def\E` → `{body:["a","b","c"," ","d","e","f"]}`. `body` is the array of `quoted_literal_char*` matches — single-char strings, with `quoted_literal_escaped_char` producing 2-char strings that preserve the `\` and the escaped char. Consumers join the array for the literal string (`body.join("")`); semantic-aware consumers can distinguish escaped vs raw chars from element shapes. Routes through `quoted_literal`: only the atom-fallback cases of the `\Q...\E quantifier?` family table (no trailing quantifier OR single-char body OR empty body with quantifier) — the multi-piece family-table fast path goes through `piece_quoted_run_quantified` which does NOT touch `quoted_literal`, so PGEN-RGX-0074/0077 family-table cases are unchanged. Picked `quoted_literal` over leaf-char atoms (literal/dot/whitespace_literal) because typing leaf chars inflates AST size 4× for the most common case; `quoted_literal` is lower volume and higher value. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.47` → `1.1.48`; contract `1.1.49` → `1.1.50`. New "Release 1.1.48 / Contract 1.1.50" section in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md). Tracker note (2026-05-01): **regex.ebnf slice 16 of N — escape subtree continues (octal).** `octal_escape` per-branch typed `{type:"escape", kind:"octal", digits:<octal-string>}`. Removed duplicate inline `octal_digits` definition (was defined twice; canonical version stays in the char-categories section). Empirical: `\o{777}` → `{type:"escape",kind:"octal",digits:"777"}`; `\o{7777}` → `{digits:"7777"}`; `\o{1}` → `{digits:"1"}`; `[\377]` (in class via `class_range_escape_unit`) → class body contains `{type:"escape",kind:"octal",digits:"377"}`. **Caveat — bare `\NNN` at atom-level:** still parses as `{type:"backreference",kind:"numeric",index:NNN}` because the `backreference` branch in `atom` precedes `escape` (PEG-ordering). PCRE2 disambiguates contextually ("if NNN ≤ 9 OR NNN capture groups exist, treat as backref; else octal") which PEG can't express directly — disambiguation left to consumers via post-parse semantic analysis if/when atom-level bare-octal support is needed. Pre-existing behavior; not changed by this slice. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.45` → `1.1.46`; contract `1.1.47` → `1.1.48`. Tracker note (2026-05-01): **PGEN-RGX-0078 logged (acknowledged / deferred, non-blocking).** Methodology-correction follow-up to PGEN-RGX-0073: 0073 closed against PGEN's absolute <50µs PRIMARY target at release `1.1.30`; 0078 files the integration-side PCRE2-relative metric (RGX ROADMAP target <5x of PCRE2 compile). Live measurement (Apple M4 Pro, default macOS allocator, 5000 samples / 200 warmup): geomean PGEN parse ~218µs vs PCRE2-no-JIT ~605ns → ~360x slower than PCRE2 no-JIT, ~85x slower than PCRE2+JIT. Slowdown corpus-wide, deterministic, weakly size-correlated. Allocator gap explains ~4-7x of divergence vs PGEN release-note p50s; mimalloc adoption would still leave geomean ~50x. RGX flagged **non-blocking**. Sequenced AFTER atom-subtree typed-shape campaign — not a correctness issue, shape work doesn't change parse-time architecture. Likely resolution path: specialised regex codegen (bypass general-purpose EBNF-driven codegen for the regex profile) OR diagnostic-out-of-scope decision retiring the <5x ROADMAP target. Logged in `docs/contracts/PGEN_RELEASED_PARSER_BUG_LEDGER.md` as `REGEX-0078`. No parser release / contract bump.

Tracker note (2026-05-01): **regex.ebnf slice 13 of N — signed_digits typing (backref family fully typed end-to-end).** Direct follow-up to slice 12. `signed_digits = sign? digits -> {sign: $1, value: $2}` — numeric subroutine refs now produce typed `{sign, value}` objects instead of the raw `[<sign?>, <int>]` 2-element shape. `sign` is `"+"`/`"-"` when matched, `[]` when un-matched (consumer maps `[]` → null, same convention as greediness/negated). Tracker note (2026-05-01): **regex.ebnf slice 11 of N — named-ref cleanup (clean name strings).** Direct follow-up to slice 10 (`backreference` typing). Three grammar changes: (1) `name` rewritten from `name_start name_continue*` to a single regex literal — emits the matched name string as a clean Terminal directly (was a multi-element chain producing `[first_char, [rest_chars]]`). (2) `name_ref` (both branches `<...>` and `'...'`) annotated `-> $2` to extract just the name from the wrappers. (3) `braced_name_ref` annotated `-> $3`. Cascading effect on every consumer of `name` — backreferences (`\k<...>`/`\k{...}` → `ref:"foo"` directly), named groups (5 forms — `(?<foo>...)`/`(?'foo'...)`/`(?P<foo>...)`/etc.), python named back-refs (`(?P=foo)`), subroutine targets, and conditions all surface clean strings instead of raw character chains. Empirical: `\k<foo>` → `ref:"foo"` (was `["<", ["f", ["o", "o"]], ">"]`); `(?<bar>x)` → name as `"bar"` (was `["b", ["a", "r"]]`). `\g<name>` etc. (subroutine_ref) still emit raw `[<delim>, "name", <delim>]` wrappers — inner is clean but wrappers remain; follow-up slice will type `subroutine_ref`. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.40` → `1.1.41`; contract `1.1.42` → `1.1.43`. New "Release 1.1.41 / Contract 1.1.43" section in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md). Regex AST schema version stays `1`. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers --features ebnf_dual_run` 495 / 0. Manifest gets 3 new entries (1 `braced_name_ref` + 2 `name_ref` branches). `make regex_parser_book_gate` green. Live-book sync covers `changelog-index.md`, `schema-versioning.md` (0.15.0 row), `json-carrier.md`. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows. Atom subtree campaign progress: 4/25 alternatives directly typed; named-ref family across all consumers now emits clean string values.

Tracker note (2026-05-01): **PGEN-RGX-0077 closed** — `[$1**]` flatten-spread peels `Alternative`. RGX bug report: every multi-char `\Q...\E quantifier?` source produced one extra wrapping layer at `pattern[0][0]` (`[[<N pieces>]]` instead of the documented flat `[<N pieces>]`). Adjacent regression to PGEN-RGX-0075 on a different codegen path. Root cause: the `[$1**]` flatten-spread codegen in [rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs) did not peel `Alternative` wrapping before inspecting child content for the unwrap decision; the codegen wraps Or-rule and rule-reference branch results in `Alternative(boxed_inner)`, so for `concatenation = piece+ -> [$1**]` each piece node arrives as `Alternative(piece_inner_node)` — pre-fix the inner match saw `Alternative` and fell into the "push as-is" arm. Fix: peel `Alternative` recursively before unwrap decision, plus preventative `Json(Value::Array(_))` arm. Empirical: `\Qab*\E{2,}` → 3 pieces flat (was wrapped); `\Qabcdef\E+` → 6 pieces flat; degenerate `\Qa\E{3}` and `\Q\E{2}` unaffected (atom-fallback path); plain literal `abc`/`hello` unaffected. New regression-lock test `regex_parser_pgen_rgx_0077_quoted_run_quantified_pieces_flat_in_concatenation` pins family-table (9 shapes from bug report) — asserts piece count + atom values + quantifier-on-last-piece + no-quantifier-on-inner-pieces. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.39` → `1.1.40`; contract `1.1.41` → `1.1.42`. New "Release 1.1.40 / Contract 1.1.42" section in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md). New `REGEX-0077` row in [docs/contracts/PGEN_RELEASED_PARSER_BUG_LEDGER.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_RELEASED_PARSER_BUG_LEDGER.md). Regex AST schema version stays `1`. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers --features ebnf_dual_run` 495 / 0 (was 494 + the new test). `make regex_parser_book_gate` green; live-book sync covers `changelog-index.md`, `schema-versioning.md` (0.14.1). Per the architectural feedback this session: every shape-affecting RGX bug should leave a regression-lock test covering the FAMILY of inputs, not just the canonical reproducer — followed for both PGEN-RGX-0075 (4 shapes) and PGEN-RGX-0077 (9 shapes). Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows. RGX integration impact: PCRE2 conformance ratchet should recover ~16-case drop; no adapter changes needed since RGX was walking the documented shape.

Tracker note (2026-05-01): **regex.ebnf slice 10 of N — typed `backreference` shape.** Two grammar changes: (1) `backreference` rule's 4 branches each got per-branch typed `{type:"backreference", kind:<form>, ...}` annotations — kinds: `numeric`/`named`/`named_braced`/`subroutine`. (2) `backreference_digits` rewritten from `nonzero_digit digit*` to a regex literal `/([1-9][0-9]*)/` with `@transform: str::parse::<usize>().unwrap_or(0)` so the rule emits a typed integer (mirrors slice-1 `digits` typing). Branch 0 (numeric) carries `index:<int>` ready to use; branches 1-3 carry `ref:<raw sub-rule shape>` since `name_ref`/`braced_name_ref`/`subroutine_ref` are still un-annotated — follow-up slice will type those for clean name extraction. Empirical: `\1` → `{"type":"backreference","kind":"numeric","index":1}`; `\23` → `{"type":"backreference","kind":"numeric","index":23}`; `\g<-2>` → `{"type":"backreference","kind":"subroutine","ref":["<",["-",2],">"]}` (numeric subroutine refs already usable since digits/sign are typed leaves in the raw shape); `\k<foo>`/`\k{foo}` typed at the outer level but `ref` still raw. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.38` → `1.1.39`; contract `1.1.40` → `1.1.41`. Tracker note (2026-05-01): **regex.ebnf slice 9 of N — typed `posix_word_boundary_alias` (closes anchor family).** PCRE2's BSD-style word-boundary aliases `[[:<:]]` and `[[:>:]]` now emit the same typed `{type:"anchor", kind:<name>}` shape as the regular `anchor` rule. Joins the typed anchor family with `kind:"posix_word_start"`/`kind:"posix_word_end"`. Closes the anchor-family typing started in slice 7 — all 11 anchor variants now emit the same dispatch shape. Empirical: `[[:<:]]foo[[:>:]]` → 5 pieces with anchors as `{"type":"anchor","kind":"posix_word_start"}`/`{"type":"anchor","kind":"posix_word_end"}` (was bare 7-char terminals). Consumer-side `classify_anchor` walker collapses to a single `obj.kind` lookup with no fallback paths. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.37` → `1.1.38`; contract `1.1.39` → `1.1.40`. Tracker note (2026-05-01): **PGEN-RGX-0076 closed** — typed `posix_class` shape. RGX bug report `/Users/richarddje/Documents/github/rgx/pgen-issues/PGEN-RGX-0076.yaml` showed that every POSIX class inside `[...]` collapsed to the literal string `"[:"` because the `posix_class` rule used a placeholder annotation `-> $1` that extracted only the opening delimiter. The book chapter `rules-char-class.md` already acknowledged this as a known sub-optimal annotation. Fix: `posix_class -> {type:"posix_class", name:$3, negated:$2}` and `posix_negation -> true`. Surfaced two latent codegen bugs in [rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs): `BooleanLiteral` and `NumberLiteral` rule-level scalar paths were emitting `ParseContent::Terminal(<stringified>)` instead of typed `Json(Bool/Number)` — surfaced when `posix_negation -> true` produced the string `"true"` rather than the boolean. Both codegen sites fixed to mirror the value-extraction path. Empirical: `[[:alpha:]]` → `{"type":"posix_class","name":"alpha","negated":[]}`; `[[:^alpha:]]` → `{"type":"posix_class","name":"alpha","negated":true}`; `[[:alpha:][:digit:]]` → 2-element class_body with both POSIX classes typed and disambiguated. `negated` convention: `true` (matched `^`) or `[]` (un-matched `posix_negation?` slot — consumers map `[]` → `false`); same convention as `quantifier.greediness`. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.36` → `1.1.37`; contract `1.1.38` → `1.1.39`. New "Release 1.1.37 / Contract 1.1.39" section in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md). New `REGEX-0076` row in [docs/contracts/PGEN_RELEASED_PARSER_BUG_LEDGER.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_RELEASED_PARSER_BUG_LEDGER.md). Regex AST schema version stays `1`. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers --features ebnf_dual_run` 494 / 0. Manifest updated (posix_class entry reshaped, posix_negation entry added). `make regex_parser_book_gate` green. Live-docs sync covers `rules-char-class.md`, `examples-char-class.md`, `json-carrier.md`, `schema-versioning.md` (0.12.0), `changelog-index.md`. RGX integration impact: adapter switches from string-match-fallback (which failed with "unrecognised class_item string `[:`") to direct typed dispatch on `obj.type == "posix_class"`. Atom subtree campaign progress: 2/25 alternatives annotated.

Tracker note (2026-05-01): **regex.ebnf slice 7 of N — atom subtree starts: typed `anchor` shape.** First slice of the atom-subtree typed-shape campaign. Piece atoms for `^`/`$`/`\A`/`\Z`/`\z`/`\b`/`\B`/`\G`/`\K` now emit typed objects with semantic kind names (`start_of_line`, `word_boundary`, `keep_out`, etc.) instead of raw escape strings. Empirical: `^foo$` → 5 pieces with 1st/5th atoms = `{"type":"anchor","kind":"start_of_line"}`/`{"type":"anchor","kind":"end_of_line"}`. Kind names are stable consumer-side identifiers — they don't depend on the source escape text and won't change if PCRE2 syntax evolves. Caveat: the POSIX word-boundary aliases `[[:<:]]`/`[[:>:]]` (handled by separate `posix_word_boundary_alias` rule) still emit raw 7-char terminals; they'll join the typed family in a follow-up slice. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.35` → `1.1.36`; contract `1.1.37` → `1.1.38`. Tracker note (2026-05-01): **regex.ebnf slice 6 of N — quantifier-subtree typed-shape campaign CLOSED.** Final two grammar changes consolidate the subtree: (1) `quant_base` reshaped from per-branch `-> $1` (heterogeneous string/object output) to per-branch typed `{min, max}` for every alternative — shorthand quantifiers expand to PCRE2-equivalent bounds (`*` → `{0,null}`, `+` → `{1,null}`, `?` → `{0,1}`); counted-quantifier branch passes through via `$1`. (2) `quantifier` rule annotated `-> {type:"quantifier", min:$1.min, max:$1.max, greediness:$2}` — emits a fully typed `{type, min, max, greediness}` object directly. Consumer-visible AST shape change for the `quantifier` field on each piece: was a `[<base>, <suffix>]` 2-tuple, now a typed object (or `[]` for un-quantified pieces, unchanged). Empirical: `a*` → `{"type":"quantifier","min":0,"max":null,"greediness":[]}`; `a{2,5}+` → `{"type":"quantifier","min":2,"max":5,"greediness":"possessive"}`; pieces with no quantifier still emit `[]`. Greediness convention: `"lazy"`/`"possessive"` for matched suffixes, `[]` for un-matched (consumers map `[]` → `"greedy"` until a future slice adds an annotation-language coalesce operator). All six rules in the quantifier subtree are now annotated (`digits` typed integer, `quant_suffix` typed enum, `counted_quantifier_body` typed `{min, max}`, `counted_quantifier` `-> $3` passthrough, `quant_base` typed `{min, max}` per branch, `quantifier` typed `{type, min, max, greediness}`). Consumer-side `extract_quantifier` walker is now a six-line typed-field read. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.34` → `1.1.35`; contract `1.1.36` → `1.1.37`. New "Release 1.1.35 / Contract 1.1.37 Highlights" section in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md). Regex AST schema version stays `1`. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers --features ebnf_dual_run` 494 / 0. Manifest `rust/test_data/ast_shape_contract/regex_v1.json` — 4 `quant_base` entries reshaped (branches 0-2 from `return_scalar "$1"` to `return_object`; branch 3 unchanged); new `quantifier` entry. `make regex_parser_book_gate` green; live-docs sync covers `rules-quantifier.md`, `json-carrier.md`, `examples-quantifiers.md`, `examples-quoted-literal.md`, `walking-the-ast.md`, `rules-piece.md`, `schema-versioning.md`, `changelog-index.md`. RGX integration impact: small walker-side update from string-vs-object dispatch to typed-field read; canonical recipe in [docs/regex_parser_book/src/rules-quantifier.md](docs/regex_parser_book/src/rules-quantifier.md). Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows. Task #40 ("Annotate regex.ebnf for full AST usability") remains in-progress; quantifier subtree is now closed; next focus areas: atom subtree, character class subtree, group family.

Tracker note (2026-05-01): **PGEN-RGX-0075 closed** — typed-shape correctness for multi-piece concatenation. RGX bug report `/Users/richarddje/Documents/github/rgx/pgen-issues/PGEN-RGX-0075.yaml` showed that `concatenation = piece+ -> [$1**]` was producing only the first piece for plain inputs like `"abc"` — `"b"` and `"c"` were silently dropped from the typed AST array (RGX's lib suite collapsed to ~73% pass rate purely from this). Root cause: `$N` PositionalRef codegen in [rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs) peeled `elements[0].content.clone()` from a `Quantified` base when `captured_vars.len() == 1`, treating Quantified-bodied rules like single-element Sequence wrappers — violating the platform-book annotation-system policy that says `$1` on a Quantified body is "the whole capture group". Why the `\Q...\E` test corpus didn't catch it: `\Qab*\E{2,}` and similar produce 3 pieces correctly because `piece+` matches a SINGLE piece whose content is itself a Sequence-of-3 from `piece_quoted_run_quantified`'s annotation; the bug only surfaced on plain multi-piece concatenations that no test exercised. Fix in three codegen sites (`generate_positional_ref`, `generate_value_extraction`, `generate_quantified_extraction`): remove the Quantified peel-arm so Quantified bases fall through to `other.clone()`. Compensating grammar change: `regex = pattern -> {...}` (was `regex = pattern? -> {...}`) — the pre-fix `?` propped up the buggy auto-peel; the inner `alternative = concatenation?` already handles emptiness, so the outer `?` was redundant. New regression-lock test `regex_parser_pgen_rgx_0075_multi_piece_concatenation_surfaces_all_pieces` in [rust/src/embedding_api.rs](rust/src/embedding_api.rs) pins empirical shape for `"a"`/`"ab"`/`"abc"`/`"hello"` (asserts piece count and atom values). `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers --features ebnf_dual_run` 494 / 0 (was 493 + the new test). Empirical probe sweep confirms all of `"a"`/`"ab"`/`"abc"`/`"hello"`/`"a*"`/`"[a-z]"`/`"a|b"`/`"(abc)"`/`"\\d+"`/`"foo\\Kbar"`/`""` produce correct typed shapes with span matching input length. **Contract bump:** parser release `1.1.34` / contract `1.1.36`. New section in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md); new `REGEX-0075` entry in [docs/contracts/PGEN_RELEASED_PARSER_BUG_LEDGER.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_RELEASED_PARSER_BUG_LEDGER.md). Regex AST schema version stays `1`. Live-docs sync: regex parser book chapters [changelog-index.md (new 1.1.34 entry), schema-versioning.md (0.9.0 row), rules-top-level.md (regex = pattern, history note)] — `make regex_parser_book_gate` green. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows. RGX integration impact: consumers walking `regex.pattern[0][0]` now see every piece; RGX should bump PGEN pin and re-run their lib suite, expected recovery from 73% to baseline.

Tracker note (2026-05-01): Task #38 closed — parens-grouped-Or trailing-annotation broadcast. Codegen now correctly applies a trailing return annotation on a parens-grouped Or to every alternative inside the group, not just the first. Two extractors fixed in lockstep: `extract_rule_annotations` in [rust/src/ast_pipeline/mod.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/mod.rs) and the cross-checker `extract_declared_annotations_from_json` in [rust/src/ast_shape_contract.rs](rust/src/ast_shape_contract.rs). Both now track a `group_open_branch_stack` and remember `last_closed_group_range` at each `)`; on the immediately-following `return_*`, broadcast the annotation to that range. The disambiguation cases all behave per the principle "the trailing annotation applies to the alternatives inside the just-closed group ONLY when it directly follows the group's close" (covered: `(A|B)->ann` broadcasts; `A|B->ann` is per-branch; `A|(B|C)->ann` broadcasts to B and C only; nested groups; etc.). Empirical proof: `parseability_probe --parse-dump-ast-pretty return_annotation "'hello'"` was producing raw `Sequence` (single-quoted branch fell through to raw passthrough); now produces `Json({"type":"string","value":"hello"})` matching the double-quoted branch. Subsequent grammar refactor: `quant_base` in [grammars/regex.ebnf](grammars/regex.ebnf) flipped from slice-5's per-branch workaround `"*" -> $1 | "+" -> $1 | ...` to the factored form `( "*" | "+" | "?" | counted_quantifier ) -> $1` — semantically identical, more elegant, demonstrates the fix end-to-end. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers --features ebnf_dual_run` 493 / 0. Manifest `rust/test_data/ast_shape_contract/return_annotation_v1.json` updated with new branch=1 entry for `string_literal`. `make regex_parser_book_gate` green. Live-docs sync: regex parser book chapters [rules-quantifier.md, changelog-index.md, schema-versioning.md] reflect the factored form and the #38 fix; platform mdBook [docs/book/src/annotation-system.md](docs/book/src/annotation-system.md) gains a new "Parens-grouped Or with trailing annotation — broadcast" section adjacent to the existing "Implicit `-> $1` default" section. No contract identity bump (regex grammar shape unchanged; return_annotation grammar shape change was a buggy → correct fix not in a versioned consumer chain). Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows. Task #38 moves from `pending` to `completed`. Task #40 ("Annotate regex.ebnf for full AST usability") remains in-progress; remaining quantifier-subtree slice: `quantifier`. Then atom subtree, class subtree, etc.

Tracker note (2026-05-01): regex.ebnf annotation work — slice 5 of N (`quant_base` per-branch `-> $1` annotations). The Or rule's four branches each get an explicit positional-passthrough annotation: `"*" -> $1 | "+" -> $1 | "?" -> $1 | counted_quantifier -> $1`. JSON output is byte-identical to pre-slice-5; the change is structural (rule moves from "raw envelope via codegen default" to "annotated, Tier-2 stable"). Empirical: `a*` still produces `quantifier: ["*", []]`; `a{2,5}` still produces `quantifier: [{"min":2,"max":5}, []]`. Per-branch form chosen because the natural factored form `( ... ) -> $1` is blocked by task #38 (`extract_rule_annotations` only attributes a trailing annotation to branch 0 of a parens-grouped Or; branches 1+ silently fall through to raw passthrough — a clear contract violation that the owner has flagged for fix as the next slice). `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers --features ebnf_dual_run` 493 / 0. The `counted_quantifier` rule got `-> $3` annotation that lifts `counted_quantifier_body`'s typed `{min, max}` straight through, dropping the surrounding `{`/whitespace/`}` tokens (which carry no semantic information beyond "this is a counted quantifier" — context the surrounding `quant_base` already conveys). Tracker note (2026-05-01): Standalone regex parser mdBook landed at [docs/regex_parser_book/](docs/regex_parser_book/) — the canonical AST integration reference for downstream consumers (RGX in particular). 24 chapters covering: cold-clone build recipe, public API surface, AST envelope structure, all six `ParseContent` variants and the `Json` carrier, walking patterns, per-rule shape reference (top-level, piece + quoted-run family, quantifier subtree, atom 25-way Or with discriminator table, character class, group family, modifier subtree, escape subtree, anchors/backrefs/misc), worked examples for every regex feature (literals, quantifiers across all 7 PCRE2 forms × 3 greediness modes, char classes, groups + alternation, the `\Q...\E` family table, anchors with discriminator function, escapes with classification function), migration from the pre-1.1.30 recursive envelope, schema-versioning policy, glossary, and a release-by-release changelog index. **The book is deliberately aligned with the parser state at commit `6e5b0f23`** (PGEN-RGX-0074 fix + slices 1-2 of typed-shape work, parser release `1.1.33` / contract `1.1.35`) so RGX can pin to that PGEN tag/commit and read a book that exactly describes the AST it observes; alignment-forward to the post-slice-3+4 state will land in a follow-up commit. RGX consumes the book via the PGEN submodule — either reads the `.md` source files at `<pgen-checkout>/docs/regex_parser_book/src/*.md` directly off disk, or browses the rendered HTML at `<pgen-checkout>/docs/regex_parser_book-html/index.html` (also accessible via github.com web UI). No build step required on the RGX side. Build path: `make regex_parser_book_gate` (uses `mdbook build docs/regex_parser_book` and writes HTML to sibling `docs/regex_parser_book-html/`). **Both source markdown AND rendered HTML are TRACKED in git** so the book is browsable directly on GitHub without requiring mdbook installation — diverges from the platform book's `docs/book-html/` gitignored convention specifically because RGX integration needs github.com browsability. Gate script `rust/scripts/regex_parser_book_gate.sh` checks the chapter set and asserts the build passes. Integration contract document now has a `## Companion Documentation` section pointing to the book. No parser code changes; no contract identity bump. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows. Task #45 ("Create regex parser mdBook for RGX as canonical AST reference") moves to `Done`. Task #40 ("Annotate regex.ebnf for full AST usability") remains in-progress.

Tracker note (2026-04-30): regex.ebnf annotation work — slice 3 of N (`counted_quantifier_body` typed `{min, max}` shape) + new `null` literal primitive in the return-annotation language. The original 2-branch rule was restructured into 4 explicit branches per logical case (`{n,m}`, `{n,}`, `{n}`, `{,m}`); each branch has its own per-branch annotation producing `{min: <int>, max: <int|null>}`. The `null` literal is JSON's sixth value type — added to the return-annotation language alongside object/array/string/number/boolean (`UnifiedReturnAST::NullLiteral`, codegen lowers to `serde_json::Value::Null`, grammar surface `null_literal := 'null' -> {type: "null"}`). Also fixed a related papercut: `NumberLiteral` codegen now preserves integer typing when the literal has no fractional part, so `{min: 0, ...}` produces `"min": 0` instead of `"min": 0.0`. Empirical: `a{2,5}` → `{"min":2,"max":5}`; `a{2,}` → `{"min":2,"max":null}`; `a{2}` → `{"min":2,"max":2}`; `a{,5}` → `{"min":0,"max":5}`. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers --features ebnf_dual_run` 493 passed. No contract bump on this commit — bump and ledger entry land on the slice that closes the quantifier subtree (`quant_base` and `quantifier` rules). Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows. Task #40 ("Annotate regex.ebnf for full AST usability") remains in-progress; remaining quantifier-subtree slices: `counted_quantifier`, `quant_base`, `quantifier`. Then atom subtree, class subtree, etc.

Tracker note (2026-04-30): regex.ebnf annotation work — slice 2 of N (`quant_suffix` typed string) + retroactive contract bumps + ledger cleanup. `quant_suffix = "?" | "+"` rewritten with per-branch annotations to emit `"lazy"` / `"possessive"` semantic strings directly. Empirical: `a*?` → `quantifier: ["*", "lazy"]` (was `["*", "?"]`). Retroactive contract bumps for the typed-shape work I had earlier (incorrectly) deferred: parser `1.1.32` / contract `1.1.34` for slice 1 (digits → integer), parser `1.1.33` / contract `1.1.35` for slice 2 (quant_suffix → typed string). Each per-rule slice that produces a consumer-visible shape change now bumps the contract identity and adds a section in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md). Removed the `REGEX-0075` row I had previously allocated for the PGEN-RGX-0074 fix slice — per owner direction, ledger IDs aren't auto-allocated by code-side work, so that row was invalid. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 493 passed. mdbook gate green. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows. Tracker note (2026-04-30): regex.ebnf annotation work — slice 1 of N. `digits` rule rewritten from `digit+` (raw `Quantified(Terminal-per-char)` shape) to `/([0-9]+)/` paired with `@transform: str::parse::<usize>().unwrap_or(0)`. The parser now emits a typed integer directly at this rule. Empirical proof: `\Qab*\E{2,}` shows `quantifier` digit position as integer `2` instead of `[["2"]]`. Per-rule slice cadence per owner direction (one rule per slice, easy to revert any single change if it turns out wrong).
