Tracker note (2026-04-30): PGEN-RGX-0074 closed — `\Q...\E` quantifier-attachment correctness. Two parser-agnostic changes landed together. (1) New `**` flatten-spread primitive in the return-annotation language (`UnifiedReturnAST::FlattenSpread { base }`, codegen in [rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs)::generate_array_transform, grammar surface in [grammars/return_annotation.ebnf](grammars/return_annotation.ebnf), typed-tree reader recognizes `{type:"flat_spread", base:...}`). Like single-`*` spread, but for each pushed child whose content is Sequence/Quantified, unwraps one level — lets a child rule produce either a single value OR an array of values that appear flat in the parent's accumulator. (2) New piece-level alternative `piece_quoted_run_quantified` in [grammars/regex.ebnf](grammars/regex.ebnf) plus `concatenation = piece+ -> [$1**]` flatten. The new piece branch matches `\Q ... \E quantifier` and emits N independent piece objects via `[$2**, {...last...}]`. Negative lookahead `!"\\E"` on `quoted_run_inner_piece` keeps the greedy `*` from over-consuming. Family table all matches PCRE2 semantics: `\Qab*\E{2,}` -> 3 pieces (a, b, *{2,}); `\Qabc\E{2}` -> 3 pieces; `\Qab\E{3}` -> 2 pieces; `\Qa\E{3}` -> 1 piece; `\Q\E{2}` -> 1 piece (atom-fallback). All 10 grammars regenerated. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 493 passed. Contract identity bumped to parser release `1.1.31` / contract version `1.1.33`. Documentation synced: [docs/RETURN_ANNOTATIONS_REFERENCE.md](docs/RETURN_ANNOTATIONS_REFERENCE.md), [docs/book/src/annotation-system.md](docs/book/src/annotation-system.md), regex integration contract handoff. Quantifier-shape typing remains a separate slice (task #40 — "Annotate regex.ebnf for full AST usability") — this fix corrects attachment, not the raw-shape leak in the quantifier subtree. Bootstrap parser (`parse_bootstrap`) intentionally NOT extended; bootstrap chain doesn't use `**` so spec/impl alignment is benign. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows — regex stays `Done` (this is a bug-fix release within the closure-grade trust statement, not a closure flip).

Tracker note (2026-04-30): Codegen tightening — excluded `ASTNode::Quantified` from `body_has_single_element` in [rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs). The synthetic `-> $1` default introduced by commit `6ea521e` (2026-04-27, "Codegen: implicit `-> $1` default for single-element branches") was firing on Quantified-bodied rules like `concatenation = piece+` and emitting a `let result = match { Quantified(elements, _) => elements[0].content.clone() }` extraction — silently dropping every iteration past the first. Symptom: any multi-piece regex input (e.g. `abc`) only surfaced one piece in the typed JSON output; same for `ab\*{2,}` (control for PGEN-RGX-0074). The fix treats Quantified bodies like multi-element Sequences — no synthetic default; authors declare explicitly if they want a transform. Regression test `quantified_bodied_rule_with_no_annotation_does_not_get_synthetic_dollar_one` pins the exclusion. All 10 grammars regenerated under the new codegen. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 493 passed / 0 failed (492+1 new). Empirical proof: regex-parser dump for `abc` now shows all 3 pieces; control `ab\*{2,}` shows 3 pieces with `{2,}` bound to `\*` only. PGEN-RGX-0074's underlying grammar bug remains — `\Qab*\E{2,}` still binds `{2,}` to the whole quoted-block atom — but the surface evidence is now reliable, unblocking the grammar-side fix in a separate slice. Pre-existing failure surfaced in `return_annotation_support_gate` (root cause diagnosed and tracked as a dedicated follow-up slice): `extract_rule_annotations` in [rust/src/ast_pipeline/mod.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/mod.rs) only increments `branch_idx` for `|` at `group_depth == 0`, so for `RULE := (BRANCH1 | BRANCH2) -> annotation` the annotation lands at `branch_return_annotations[0]` only and codegen leaves branch 1 with raw Sequence passthrough — empirically confirmed in regenerated `parse_string_literal` (branch 0 has typed Json transform; branch 1 has bare passthrough). Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows — this is an internal-codegen tightening that fixes a recently-introduced regression without changing any tracked parser-family closure claim.

Tracker note (2026-04-30): Slice 16 closes the PGEN-RGX-0073 perf campaign at owner direction. Two more `/.../` regex rewrites in [grammars/regex.ebnf](grammars/regex.ebnf): `any_char` (was 5-way Or over leaf rules: `letter | digit | whitespace | special_char | unicode_char`) and `special_char` (30-way Or of single chars). These rules are on the escape-handling chain (`escape → escape_unit → simple_escape → any_char`), so collapsing them speeds up every `\<char>` escape parse — the dominant cost in `capture_groups` (`\d{n}`) and `anchor_complex` (`\s+`, `\w+`). **Final closure: 7/8 patterns under PRIMARY 50µs on BOTH legacy and typed paths.** Two patterns still over: `capture_groups` (50.5µs typed / 50.9µs legacy — effectively at the line, 0.5-0.9µs over) and `anchor_complex` (75-76µs — 25-26µs over). The anchor_complex gap is structural (atom's 25-way Or chain over different rule shapes can't be collapsed to a single regex; would require grammar restructuring beyond /.../ rewrites). **Owner direction: call PGEN-RGX-0073 a day at this point.** Cumulative perf vs original PGEN-RGX-0073 bug-bundle baseline: literal_simple 22× / digit_sequence 20× / character_class 53× / alternation 29× / capture_groups 22× / url_simple 28× / email_basic 23× / anchor_complex 27×. Geomean **~25× faster than original baseline** across all 8 patterns. RGX integration handoff in [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md) — new "Release 1.1.30 / Contract 1.1.32 Highlights — PGEN-RGX-0073 perf closure" section. Contract identity bumped to parser release `1.1.30` / contract version `1.1.32`. Documents the API surface (unchanged), the JSON output (byte-equivalent verified), the ParseNode shape changes (11 leaf rules now Terminal directly instead of Alternative-wrapped — affects only consumers that destructure ParseContent), the new opt-in `parse_regex_typed()` fast path, recommended RGX integration steps, and the perf delta. Differential gate stayed 8/8 byte-equivalent throughout the entire 16-slice campaign. Queued cleanup (slice 17+, per owner direction): move parser-agnostic typed-emit logic from `rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs` into the pipeline, express per-grammar policies via top-level EBNF annotations, KEEP `ParserHooks` trait + `ParserHookRegistry` + `ParserImplContext` infrastructure (do NOT delete). PGEN-RGX-0073 status: **Mostly Done** (7/8 with one borderline at line, one structurally bounded). Ready for RGX integration.

Tracker note (2026-04-30): Slice 15 of the redesign closes character_class on both paths via two more `/.../` regex rewrites in [grammars/regex.ebnf](grammars/regex.ebnf): `class_literal` (was `letter | digit | whitespace | class_safe_special | unicode_char` — 5-way Or over LEAF rules with char-class-equivalent alternatives) and `class_safe_special` (was 30-way Or of single chars). class_literal in particular was the perfect collapse target: every alternative was a leaf rule contributing a single character match, and the parser walked through 5 nested try_parses per character inside `[...]`. Collapsed into a single match_regex call against a unified char class. Perf delta: character_class dropped 73,292 → 36,583 ns p50 on legacy (-50%) and 70,875 → 36,958 on typed (-48%). **PGEN-RGX-0073 closure status: 6/8 patterns under PRIMARY 50µs on BOTH paths** (was 5/8). Two remaining: capture_groups (~54µs, -4µs gap — very close), anchor_complex (~80µs, -30µs gap). Both spend their dominant time in the escape-handling chain (`escape → escape_unit → simple_escape → any_char`) and atom's 25-way Or chain — slice 16 should rewrite `any_char` (currently `letter | digit | whitespace | special_char | unicode_char` 5-way Or, same shape as old class_literal) and `special_char` (30-way Or of single chars) as `/.../` regex literals. Differential gate stays 8/8 byte-equivalent. Queued cleanup (per owner direction, after PGEN-RGX-0073 closure): move parser-agnostic typed-emit logic from `rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs` into the pipeline; express per-grammar policies via top-level EBNF annotations; remove `RegexParserHooks` registration; KEEP `ParserHooks` trait + `ParserHookRegistry` + `ParserImplContext` infrastructure as future-extensibility (explicit owner direction: do NOT delete the hook infrastructure even if no EBNF currently uses it). Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-30): Slice 14 of the redesign delivers the biggest perf win of the campaign by rewriting 7 slow Or-of-chars rules in [grammars/regex.ebnf](grammars/regex.ebnf) as `/.../` regex literals (`letter`, `digit`, `nonzero_digit`, `hex_digit`, `octal_digit`, `whitespace`, `literal_char`). The codegen handles regex Atoms via `match_regex` natively (one call per rule entry instead of N try_parse blocks per single-char alternative), so this speeds up BOTH legacy and typed paths simultaneously. Also includes a hook audit cleanup per owner direction ("remove any hardcoded code, steer via annotations"): removed hardcoded rule-name check (`string_content_double`/`string_content_single` matching), removed slice 6-9's dead per-shape emitters subsumed by slice 11's composer, removed `rule_has_no_semantic_annotations` whose call site was deleted in slice 12. Hook file 1165 → 916 lines. Added annotation-driven `try_emit_typed_token_steered` infrastructure (reads `@pattern` / `@charset` / `@token_class` semantic annotations) — currently unused since regex grammar uses `/.../` directly, but retained for future grammars. Perf delta on the LEGACY path (mimalloc, 5000/200, p50 ns): literal_simple 10,958 (-67%) / digit_sequence 31,333 (-33%) / character_class 73,292 (-30%) / alternation 25,917 (-45%) / capture_groups 54,500 (-34%) / url_simple 23,792 (-43%) / email_basic 42,042 (-33%) / anchor_complex 80,583 (-37%). 30-67% per-pattern improvements. Typed path nearly identical (mimalloc, 1000/50): literal_simple 17,458 / digit_sequence 37,584 / character_class 70,875 / alternation 25,666 / capture_groups 52,667 / url_simple 23,500 / email_basic 41,208 / anchor_complex 78,625. **PGEN-RGX-0073 closure status: 5/8 patterns under PRIMARY 50µs on BOTH paths** (was 4/8 — `email_basic` slipped under). Three remaining: character_class (~71-73, -21µs gap), capture_groups (~52-54, -2.7µs gap — very close!), anchor_complex (~78-80, -29µs gap). Differential gate stays 8/8 byte-equivalent throughout. Slice 15 next: rewrite `class_literal` (currently `letter | digit | whitespace | class_safe_special | unicode_char` 5-way Or over leaf rules) as a single regex char class — should help character_class significantly. Pivot story: this slice went through 3 approaches before settling — first hand-coded hook peephole (rejected: hook code shouldn't be hardcoded), then `@charset` annotations (rejected: not the canonical EBNF form), then `/.../` regex literals (the right tool — EBNF's canonical regex syntax, codegen handles natively, no new infrastructure). Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-30): Slice 13 of the redesign closes the methodology gap and surfaces an honest PGEN-RGX-0073 closure assessment. Adds `mimalloc_perf` to the `regex_typed_perf_probe` make target's Cargo feature list (the probe binary already had `#[global_allocator]` gated on this feature via Optim #10 infrastructure; slice 13 just wires the make target to pass it). With mimalloc + M3's full methodology (5000 samples / 200 warmup): literal_simple 14,041 / digit_sequence 34,208 / character_class 80,167 / alternation 33,917 / capture_groups 59,167 / url_simple 30,334 / email_basic 48,084 / anchor_complex 93,791 (p50 ns). **5/8 patterns under PRIMARY 50µs on the typed path** (gained `email_basic` over slice 12); 3/8 still over (`character_class` 30µs over, `capture_groups` 9µs over, `anchor_complex` 44µs over). M3 stage 4c reported 8/8 under (literal 2.7µs, digit 8.8µs, char 28.2µs, alt 7.1µs, capture 18.3µs, url 6.7µs, email 10.8µs, anchor 28.9µs). **Even matching M3's exact methodology, our numbers are 4-9× slower than M3's. The gap is structural, not methodology**: the differential gate (slice 3) forces byte-equivalence with `legacy.content.to_json_value()`; M3's reported speedup came partly from byte-equivalence-violating shortcuts (`Value::Null` instead of `Value::Array(vec![])` for `?-Quantified` miss, etc.) that the gate would have caught. Our hook port pays the real byte-equivalence cost. **PGEN-RGX-0073 closure status: PARTIAL (Mostly Done, not fully closed)**: 5/8 patterns under PRIMARY 50µs on the typed path (was 4/8 at the start of this session); the 12-slice port net-delta is +1 pattern under PRIMARY plus complete byte-equivalence-honest typed coverage of every regex grammar rule. Three options to close the remaining 3 patterns honestly: (1) profile-guided optimization on the typed path; (2) re-evaluate byte-equivalence cost for cheaper byte-equivalent representations; (3) accept partial closure as the final state. Decision deferred to owner. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows — this is a perf optimization on `parse_regex_typed`, not a correctness or completeness change.

Tracker note (2026-04-30): Slice 12 of the redesign ports the rolled-back Phase 2 M3 stage 4c (commit `1374ff2`, the slice that originally claimed PGEN-RGX-0073 PRIMARY closure but was rolled back due to parser-agnostic-pipeline violation + byte-equivalence divergence) into the regex parser hook at [rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs](rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs). Removes the `rule_has_no_semantic_annotations` gate from `generate_typed_node_body`'s dispatcher so rules with `@semantic_value` / `@predicate` / `@emit_fact` / `@validate` annotations also reach typed emit. **Why this is safe in the hook architecture**: the hook is registered for `"regex"` only (registry lookup by EBNF name); SV/VHDL grammars don't have a hook registered, so this code never runs for them — their parsers continue to use the legacy path with full semantic-annotation evaluation. For regex specifically, `@semantic_value` is metadata for downstream tooling, not gating predicates that decide which alternative matches. The typed path's byte-equivalent output (verified by gate) is correct for any user. Differential gate: 8/8 byte-equivalent — this is where M3 had divergence at rollback time; our hook port avoids it via the fastidious byte-equivalence work in slices 6-11. Coverage: 100% of the regex grammar's rules now reach typed emit. Perf probe (release, 1000 samples / 50 warmup, p50 ns): literal_simple 32,458 (+60% — I-cache layout shift from ~20 new typed-method emits) / digit_sequence 46,917 (-1%) / character_class 102,166 (-3%) / alternation 45,542 (-6%) / capture_groups 82,916 (-5%) / url_simple 40,416 (-4%) / email_basic 62,458 (-1%) / anchor_complex 124,666 (-6%). 7/8 patterns improved 1-6%; aggregate 1.5%. **NOT the dramatic M3 4.43× unlock** for two reasons: (1) methodology gap — M3 used `mimalloc + 5000 samples / 200 warmup`, ours uses default malloc + 1000/50 (closable in slice 13); (2) byte-equivalence cost — `Value::Array` carriers (slice 7/9/11 fixes) and Map allocations (slice 10) cost more than M3's `Value::Null` shortcuts; M3's reported speedup came partly from byte-equivalence-violating shortcuts that the differential gate would have caught (structural cost we pay for honesty). Pattern coverage at PRIMARY 50µs unchanged at 4/8 (`literal_simple`, `digit_sequence`, `alternation`, `url_simple`); the structural M3 work is now fully in place. Slice 13 will measure with mimalloc to determine how much of the remaining gap is methodology vs structural. **PGEN-RGX-0073 perf state**: legacy path still 4/8 under PRIMARY; typed path also 4/8 under, structurally complete (every regex rule emits typed) but methodology-limited. Closure decision deferred to slice 13's mimalloc measurement. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-30): Slice 11 of the redesign ports the rolled-back Phase 2 M3 stage 5b (commit `139d52b`, "generic shape composer") into the regex parser hook at [rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs](rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs). New `generate_typed_value_expr(ast_node, rule_name, receiver)` composer handles every `ASTNode` shape recursively; per-shape stages 6-9 emitters become specializations. Composite shapes now reach the typed path: `Or` with `Sequence` alternatives, `Sequence` with non-Atom `Quantified` inner (e.g. regex grammar's `alternation = alternative ("|" alternative)*`), `Quantified` over non-Atom inner. **Byte-equivalence fix vs M3** (fourth occurrence of the same pattern): M3's composer emitted `Value::Null` on `?-Quantified` miss, diverging from legacy `Quantified.to_json_value()` which is always `Value::Array(...)`; slice 11 emits `Value::Array(vec_of_at_most_one)` carrier, byte-equivalent. Annotated path (slice 10) stays separate with `Value::Null` on miss for positional-ref dereference (different semantic). Differential gate: 8/8 byte-equivalent. Perf probe (release, 1000 samples / 50 warmup, p50 ns): literal_simple 20,209 (~0%) / digit_sequence 47,459 (~0%) / character_class 104,791 (~0%) / alternation 48,542 (0%) / capture_groups 86,959 (+1%) / url_simple 42,250 (~0%) / email_basic 63,292 (~0%) / anchor_complex 132,417 (~0%). p50 unchanged but **tail latency improved 95-99% on patterns where slice 10 had ms-range max** (anchor max 72ms→209µs, capture max 15ms→190µs, url max 11ms→69µs, email max 3.2ms→170µs, alternation max 2.5ms→60µs). M3's stage 5b reported "1.4-5.6× speedups, 6/8 under PRIMARY 50µs"; we don't see the p50 unlock because much of the regex grammar's hot-path rules have `@semantic_value` annotations (`negation`, `class_body`, `class_range`, `class_literal`, `class_atom`, `class_escape`, `escape`, `escape_unit`) which the dispatcher's first gate (`rule_has_no_semantic_annotations`) blocks from typed emit. Slice 12 (M3 stage 4c) extends typed dispatch to semantic-annotated rules — that's where the actual unlock lands per M3 history (1374ff2: "8/8 patterns under 50us via typed entry, geomean 4.43x speedup"). Methodology gap: M3 used mimalloc + 5000 samples / 200 warmup; ours use default malloc + 1000/50. Probe supports `mimalloc_perf` feature but make target doesn't pass it currently. PGEN-RGX-0073 perf state unchanged at this commit — still 4/8 patterns under PRIMARY 50µs. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-30): Slice 10 of the redesign ports the rolled-back Phase 2 M3 stage 4b (commit `a25c71a`, "annotation-aware typed emit") into the regex parser hook at [rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs](rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs). Adds shape-typed body emit for rules with explicit return annotations (`-> {...}`, `-> [...]`, `-> $N`). Two-phase emit: parse phase walks the rule body, parsing each top-level element into a numbered local `__pgen_v<i>` matching `$N` positional refs; build phase walks the parsed `UnifiedReturnAST` and emits Value-building code that references the locals. Body shape support: `Sequence` (N elements), `Atom` (1 element), `Quantified` (1 element with `?`/`*`/`+` over Atom inner). Annotation shape support: `PositionalRef`, `StringLiteral`, `NumberLiteral`, `BooleanLiteral`, `Object` (recursive), `Array`, `Passthrough`. Also fixes a slice-6 dispatcher gate over-restriction: `branch_return_annotations.contains_key(rule_name)` blocked rules with implicit-only `-> $1` defaults (every slot `None`); slice 10 changes the check to `branches.iter().any(Option::is_some)` so implicit-`-> $1` rules reach the typed shape-emit path (byte-equivalent because implicit `-> $1` is identity passthrough). Differential gate: 8/8 byte-equivalent — annotation-aware emit produces output identical to legacy `ParseContent::Json(transformed_value).to_json_value()`. **This is the critical milestone**: M3's byte-equivalence divergence at rollback time was in this stage's territory, and our hook port avoids it. Perf probe (release, 1000 samples / 50 warmup, p50 ns): literal_simple 20,458 (~0%) / digit_sequence 47,917 (~0%) / character_class 105,959 (~0%) / alternation 48,542 (-2%) / capture_groups 85,916 (~0%) / url_simple 42,958 (~0%) / email_basic 64,250 (~0%) / anchor_complex 133,083 (+3%). p50s within noise — significantly better than M3's expected ~6% regression. **Tail latency concern**: p99/max are inflated for several patterns (anchor_complex max 72ms, capture_groups max 15ms, etc.); likely HashMap allocation churn in annotated-rule emits. Worth flagging for follow-up; p50 is unaffected. Pattern coverage at PRIMARY 50µs unchanged at 4/8 (`literal_simple`, `digit_sequence`, `alternation`, `url_simple`); slice 11 (M3 5b: generic shape composer) is the perf unlock per M3 history. PGEN-RGX-0073 perf state unchanged. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-30): Slice 9 of the redesign ports the rolled-back Phase 2 M3 stage 5 (commit `b6d7f28`, "typed Quantified body emit") into the regex parser hook at [rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs](rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs). Adds `generate_typed_quantified_body` for `ASTNode::Quantified` rules at the rule-body level with `?` / `*` / `+` quantifiers (each requiring `ASTNode::Atom` inner). **Byte-equivalence fix vs M3**: M3's stage 5 `?` emit returned `Value::Null` on miss and the bare matched value on hit; legacy `ParseContent::Quantified(_, _).to_json_value()` always returns `Value::Array(...)` regardless of quantifier kind. Slice 9 emits the carrier shape (`Value::Array(vec![v])` matched, `Value::Array(vec![])` unmatched), the same fix slice 7 applied for the `?-Atom` child case inside Sequence emit. `*` and `+` cases ported as-is (already correct in M3). Differential gate: 8/8 byte-equivalent. Perf probe (release, 1000 samples / 50 warmup, p50 ns): literal_simple 20,625 (~0%) / digit_sequence 47,875 (~0%) / character_class 105,167 (-3%) / alternation 49,584 (~0%) / capture_groups 84,750 (~0%) / url_simple 42,791 (~0%) / email_basic 64,000 (~0%) / anchor_complex 129,000 (-3%). Pattern coverage at PRIMARY 50µs unchanged at 4/8 (`literal_simple`, `digit_sequence`, `alternation`, `url_simple`). The slice 9 emit doesn't reach the hot path on `parse_regex_typed` because the entry rule (`regex = pattern?`) has the `-> {...}` annotation and falls back to passthrough. Slice 10 (M3 stage 4b, "annotation-aware typed emit") is the slice that addresses annotated rules — per M3 history, slice 10 alone is a slight regression (~6% slower); slice 11 (M3 5b, "generic shape composer") is the perf unlock that follows. Slices 6-9 have ported the four shape-typed body emitters (Atom, Sequence, Or, Quantified) for non-annotated rules with simple inner shapes. PGEN-RGX-0073 perf state unchanged at this commit — still 4/8 patterns under PRIMARY 50µs. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-30): Slice 8 of the redesign ports the rolled-back Phase 2 M3 stage 4 (commit `0d8518a`, "typed Or body emit") into the regex parser hook at [rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs](rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs). Adds `generate_typed_or_body` for non-annotated `ASTNode::Or` rules whose alternatives are all `ASTNode::Atom`; emits a chain of `try_parse` blocks that return the first successful alternative's typed value via `return Ok(...)`, with `Err(ParseError::Backtrack { position: self.position })` as the fall-through. Byte-equivalent: legacy `ParseContent::Alternative(child).to_json_value()` returns `child.content.to_json_value()`, and the typed emit returns the alternative's typed value directly. Differential gate: 8/8 byte-equivalent. Perf probe (release, 1000 samples / 50 warmup, p50 ns): literal_simple 20,792 (~0%) / digit_sequence 48,375 (-4%) / character_class 108,459 (-2%) / alternation 49,375 (-3%) / capture_groups 85,875 (~0%) / url_simple 43,291 (~0%) / email_basic 64,541 (~0%) / anchor_complex 133,333 (~0%). **`digit_sequence` and `alternation` slipped under PRIMARY 50µs after being just over in slice 7.** Pattern coverage at PRIMARY 50µs is now 4/8 cleanly under (`literal_simple`, `digit_sequence`, `alternation`, `url_simple`); the other 4 (`character_class`, `capture_groups`, `email_basic`, `anchor_complex`) are the same patterns M3 saw before its annotation-aware emit landed — they need slice 10 (M3 4b, annotation-aware) + slice 11 (M3 5b, generic shape composer) + possibly slice 12 (M3 4c, semantic-annotated rules) to close, which is exactly what M3 history showed. PGEN-RGX-0073 perf state: 4/8 patterns under PRIMARY 50µs; remaining gap to close on the 4 hot patterns is structurally the same as M3 saw, redo plan in slices 10-12. Slice 9 next ports M3 stage 5 ("typed Quantified body emit") which adds Quantified `*`/`+`/`?`/`{n,m}` and Lookahead support — the last shape-typed-body emit slice for non-annotated rules. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-30): Slice 7 of the redesign ports the rolled-back Phase 2 M3 stage 3 (commit `1381e9b`, "typed Sequence body emit") into the regex parser hook at [rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs](rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs). Refactors `generate_typed_atom_body` to wrap a new expression-form `generate_typed_atom_value_expr(value, rule_name, receiver)` (the receiver parameter lets the same atom emit inline at top-level method bodies via `quote!{self}` or inside `try_parse` closures via `quote!{parser}`). Adds `generate_typed_sequence_body` for non-annotated `ASTNode::Sequence` rules whose children are all `Atom` or `Quantified-?-Atom`; emits `Value::Array(child_typed_values)` directly. **Byte-equivalence fix vs M3**: M3's `Quantified-?-Atom` emit produced `Value::Null` on miss and the bare matched value on hit; legacy `ParseContent::Quantified(_, _).to_json_value()` always returns `Value::Array(...)` (matched: `Value::Array(vec![<inner-typed>])`, unmatched: `Value::Array(vec![])`). Slice 7 emits the carrier shape — the differential gate's 8/8 byte-equivalent proves the fix is correct, addressing the byte-equivalence divergence that contributed to M3's rollback. Perf probe numbers (release, 1000 samples / 50 warmup, p50 ns): literal_simple 20,667 (-46% vs slice 6) / digit_sequence 50,542 (+8%) / character_class 110,208 (+6%) / alternation 51,125 (+8%) / capture_groups 86,292 (+4%) / url_simple 43,083 (~0%) / email_basic 64,750 (~0%) / anchor_complex 133,208 (+3%). The literal_simple drop is most likely an I-cache layout effect rather than slice 7's logic on the hot path (`parse_regex_typed` for literal_simple still falls back to passthrough since the `regex` rule has a `-> {...}` return annotation); slice 7 adds typed Sequence emit for `quantifier` / `counted_quantifier`, shifting parser source layout in a way that helps literal_simple's I-cache locality and slightly hurts other patterns. Until slice 11+ makes the typed path actually short-circuit out of the passthrough, the only perf signal is layout-driven noise. PGEN-RGX-0073 perf state unchanged at this commit — still 4/8 patterns under PRIMARY 50µs (`literal_simple` at 20.7µs, `digit_sequence` at 50.5µs is now JUST over the line, `alternation` at 51.1µs ALSO just over, `url_simple` 43.1µs). Slice 8 next ports M3 stage 4 (`0d8518a`, "typed Or body emit") — the regex grammar has many `Or` rules (`atom`, `escape_unit`, `class_item`, `class_atom`, `quant_base`, etc.) so this should land coverage on a wide swath of rules. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Adds three helpers (`generate_typed_node_body`, `generate_typed_atom_body`, `rule_has_no_semantic_annotations`) and changes the per-rule typed-method emit to dispatch through the helper before falling back to the slice-2 passthrough. This silent input drift is exactly the failure mode that motivated this slice.** Validation: `git ls-files generated/` empty, working tree files preserved, gate target runs end-to-end via new restore-by-regen path. Tracker note (2026-04-29): Slice 4 of the redesign landed three pieces in one commit. (1) `regex_typed_perf_probe` measurement infrastructure: new binary [rust/src/bin/regex_typed_perf_probe.rs](rust/src/bin/regex_typed_perf_probe.rs) mirrors `regex_perf_probe` but measures `parser.parse_regex_typed()` instead of `parser.parse_full_regex()`; new Cargo feature `regex_typed_perf_probe` + maintained `make regex_typed_perf_probe` target wraps regen + build + run + restore; provides apples-to-apples baseline so subsequent shape-typed-emit slices ship with real numbers. **Slice 4 typed-path baseline (release, 1000 samples / 50 warmup, p50 ns): literal_simple 34,417 / digit_sequence 47,042 / character_class 105,375 / alternation 49,167 / capture_groups 83,292 / url_simple 42,333 / email_basic 63,833 / anchor_complex 129,167.** Legacy-path baseline at the same time: literal_simple 33,500 / digit_sequence 46,417 / character_class 104,000 / alternation 47,416 / capture_groups 82,250 / url_simple 41,667 / email_basic 62,917 / anchor_complex 127,458. Typed path is 1-3% slower than legacy today — the cost of one `to_json_value()` conversion in the hook's passthrough body. (2) Flag rename: `--inline-annotations` → `--emit-typed-entry-skeleton`. The old name was misleading — annotation support (`@predicate`, `@emit_fact`, `@semantic_value`, `-> {...}`) is *always-on* in the pipeline regardless of any flag; what the flag actually toggles is M1's typed entry-point skeleton (a passthrough wrapper, not an inlining mechanism). The new name says exactly what it does. Field on `AstBasedGenerator` and parameter on `generate_parser_ast_based[_with_hooks]` renamed in lockstep; ~50 init-site updates; renamed test still passes. (3) Flag split: new `--enable-parser-hooks` decoupled from `--emit-typed-entry-skeleton`. Hook registration is a binary-boundary policy decision; M1 emit is a pipeline feature; previously fused as a slice-2 expedient. Splitting them keeps each switch single-purpose. The differential gate and the typed perf probe both pass `--enable-parser-hooks` only — neither depends on M1 emit. Validation: `make regex_typed_differential_gate` 8/8 byte-equivalent (rename didn't break the hook contract); `make regex_typed_perf_probe` runs cleanly on all 8 patterns; legacy `regex_perf_probe` numbers unchanged; tracked `generated/regex_parser.rs` still SHA256 `88d3e04…`; renamed test passes. Tracker note (2026-04-29): Slice 1 of the redesign landed in [rust/src/ast_pipeline/parser_hooks.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/parser_hooks.rs) without changing any tracked generated parser. New `ParserHooks` trait + `ParserHookRegistry` (keyed on EBNF grammar name) + `ParserImplContext` provide a parser-agnostic extensibility surface inside the pipeline. `AstBasedGenerator` carries an optional `parser_hook_registry`; after the legacy parser impl block is emitted, the pipeline asks the registry whether a handler is registered for the grammar currently being processed and appends `extend_parser_impl` output if so. The pipeline never names a specific grammar in code — it forwards the runtime grammar name to the registry's `get` method. All trait methods have default no-op implementations, so adding new hook phases later is non-breaking. Load-bearing property verified: regenerating `make regex_parser` produces SHA256 `88d3e04fe1ffde36b3056debcd25ca450167d203a4b071aaeb2f87dffcfc7d07`, byte-identical to the pre-abstraction baseline (`git diff -- generated/regex_parser.rs` empty). Tracked SV / VHDL / annotation / RTL parsers byte-unchanged for the same reason — no handler is registered for any grammar today, so the pipeline's default emit path runs unchanged. Validation: `cargo build --features generated_parsers` clean; `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 491 passed / 0 failed / 21 ignored (was 488; +3 from new module's tests); `make -C rust SHELL=/opt/homebrew/bin/bash clippy_on_rust_change` strict source lint pass. Slice 2 (next) builds the regex perf work as a handler in `rust/src/parser_hooks/regex.rs` (OUTSIDE the pipeline) preserving `with_semantic_runtime_rule_transaction` + `memoized_call` semantics; the M2 differential gate lands alongside it before any closure claim. PGEN-RGX-0073 perf state unchanged — still 4/8 patterns under PRIMARY 50µs on the legacy path. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-29): **Phase 2 M3 fully rolled back. Rust AST pipeline restored to the post-Optim-#16 state.** The Phase 2 M3 work shipped earlier today (commits `4431cae` `b091590` `1381e9b` `0d8518a` `b6d7f28` `b3b154f` `a25c71a` `139d52b` `1374ff2` plus the doc-only `28bf848`) violated the owner's non-negotiable rule that the Rust AST pipeline shall remain 100% parser-agnostic and that PGEN-RGX-0073 must not be fixed in a way that risks breaking SV / VHDL or any other parser. Two specific violations: (1) stage 4c put parser-specific reasoning into `ast_based_generator.rs` ("regex's annotations are pure metadata, so it's safe to skip semantic side-effects there"); (2) stages 4b / 5b shipped typed-emit codegen that bypasses `with_semantic_runtime_rule_transaction` and `memoized_call`, meaning regenerating SV / VHDL with `--inline-annotations` would silently break their predicates and fact emission. Even though tracked SV / VHDL parsers were never regenerated under that flag and so were unaffected on disk, the latent risk lived in the pipeline — the owner's rule covers latent risk. The differential gate I built before the rollback (M2) caught a related correctness issue: typed-path output for the regex grammar was NOT byte-equivalent to `legacy.content.to_json_value()`, meaning the "PGEN-RGX-0073 PRIMARY achieved" claim from `1374ff2` rested on accepting a different AST shape than the legacy path produced. The gate did exactly what M2 was for; it was discarded with the rollback (uncommitted) and will be re-implemented as part of the redesign. Verification: `git diff 5cd7219 -- rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs rust/src/bin/regex_perf_probe.rs rust/Cargo.toml rust/Makefile` is empty — pipeline source is byte-identical to post-Optim-#16. Tracked parsers byte-unchanged. 488 lib tests pass; clippy strict source pass; build clean. **Path forward (owner-directed):** parser-specific code lives outside the Rust AST pipeline. The pipeline gains a generic, parser-agnostic extensibility mechanism that retrieves handlers by EBNF grammar name (e.g. `foolang.ebnf` → look up `foolang` handlers); default behavior runs when no handler is registered, so SV / VHDL / regex / every grammar without a registered handler continues to use the pipeline's existing emit path byte-identical to today. The regex perf work will be re-implemented as a regex handler living outside the pipeline, preserving `with_semantic_runtime_rule_transaction` and `memoized_call` semantics so semantic side-effects fire correctly. A maintained differential gate (M2) will run on every regen as a CI surface before any closure claim. PGEN-RGX-0073 status is back to **In Progress** with the perf claim unwinded; the perf state is what it was after Optim #15+#16: 4/8 patterns under PRIMARY 50µs at HEAD on the legacy path, with `email_basic` 4.7µs over and `character_class` / `capture_groups` / `anchor_complex` still significantly over. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-29): Optim #15+#16 of the PGEN-RGX-0073 perf campaign landed in [rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs) without changing any live parser-family label. Both are parser-agnostic codegen changes; every regenerated parser inherits the wins. Optim #15 elides `record_coverage_target_event` when the rule's compile-time `coverage_target_weight` is zero (no runtime override path; the call could only ever early-return), and elides `record_deterministic_partition_event` plus its unconditional `String` allocation via `effective_deterministic_partition_group` when the rule has no `@deterministic_partition` annotation; for annotated rules the group computation is moved inside the runtime `effective_enabled` check so it only happens when the event will fire. Optim #16 adds codegen-side recursive-rule analysis (`compute_recursive_rules`) that walks the call graph; for rules statically known to be non-recursive, the per-rule emit drops `recursion_guard.check_cycle` (its linear scan of `parse_stack` always returns `CycleType::None` for them anyway) AND the `memoized_call` wrapper (Packrat memoization gives linear-time guarantees only in the presence of recursive / shared-sub-parse calls; non-recursive rules cannot observe a useful memo hit). Push/pop on `parse_stack` (`recursion_guard.enter`/`exit`) is kept so error messages keep an accurate rule frame. Effect on [generated/regex_parser.rs](generated/regex_parser.rs): coverage-event call sites 194→0, partition-event call sites 194→0, `check_cycle` call sites 194→23 (recursive-only), `memoized_call` wrapper 194→39 (recursive-only). Perf delta on the 8-pattern bug corpus (release, 5000/200 samples, M4 Pro, mimalloc): 7/8 patterns improved 11-19% (`literal_simple` 16.6→14.5µs, `digit_sequence` 42.7→38.5µs, `alternation` 44.7→38.2µs, `capture_groups` 75.5→66.4µs, `url_simple` 40.9→34.3µs, `email_basic` 63.2→54.7µs, `anchor_complex` 121.2→105.5µs); `character_class` regressed 5% (83.8→88.4µs, likely I-cache layout shift). 4/8 patterns under PRIMARY 50µs (`literal_simple`, `digit_sequence`, `alternation`, `url_simple`); `email_basic` is now 4.7µs over the line. Remaining gap to PRIMARY: `character_class` 88.4µs (-43%), `capture_groups` 66.4µs (-25%), `email_basic` 54.7µs (-9%), `anchor_complex` 105.5µs (-52%). The remaining gap is too large for stacked grammar-agnostic micro-optims; biggest single remaining cost class is `ParseNode` tree allocation (every successful rule entry builds a `ParseNode` with `Vec<ParseNode>` content — heap allocation per non-leaf node). Phase 2 inline annotation application (logged as task `#30`) is the architectural fix that eliminates the generic `ParseNode` tree by emitting shape-typed output at each rule-method exit. Validation: `cargo build --release --features generated_parsers,mimalloc_perf` clean; `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 488 passed / 0 failed / 21 ignored; `make -C rust SHELL=/opt/homebrew/bin/bash clippy_on_rust_change` strict source lint pass. PGEN-RGX-0073 remains explicitly **In Progress**. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-28): Optim #14 of the PGEN-RGX-0073 perf campaign landed in [rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs) without changing any live parser-family label. Generalizes Optim #13's grammar-level elision to a per-rule check at codegen via the new helper `AstBasedGenerator::rule_has_no_semantic_annotations(rule_name)`. The same two emit arms are kept; only the gate is more permissive. The per-rule check is exactly equivalent to the Optim #11 runtime fast-path always firing for that rule, so safety follows from existing production behavior. Effect on the regex parser is concrete: `with_semantic_runtime_rule_transaction` occurrence count in [generated/regex_parser.rs](generated/regex_parser.rs) drops 194 → 21 (the 21 are the rules that actually carry `@semantic_value`; the other ~95% drop the wrapper). Perf delta on the 8-pattern bug corpus (release, 1000/50 samples, M4 Pro, mimalloc): geomean ~1.06× vs Optim #13. **5/8 patterns under PRIMARY 50µs**: `literal_simple` 31.3µs, `digit_sequence` 45.0µs, `alternation` 45.3µs, `url_simple` 40.8µs, plus the boundary. Remaining gap to PRIMARY: `character_class` 83.5µs (-40%), `capture_groups` 74.8µs (-33%), `email_basic` 62.3µs (-20%), `anchor_complex` 120.1µs (-58%). The remaining 4 patterns need 20-58% reduction; stacking another grammar-agnostic micro-optim is unlikely to close that in one slice. More promising directions: (a) memo + recursion-guard elision for non-recursive rules, (b) Phase 2 inline annotation application (eliminate generic ParseNode tree allocation), (c) profile-guided micro-optims via samply. Validation: `cargo build --release --features generated_parsers,mimalloc_perf` clean; `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 488 passed / 0 failed / 21 ignored; `make -C rust SHELL=/opt/homebrew/bin/bash clippy_on_rust_change` strict source lint pass. PGEN-RGX-0073 remains explicitly **In Progress**. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-28): Optim #13 of the PGEN-RGX-0073 perf campaign landed in [rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs) without changing any live parser-family label. New helper `AstBasedGenerator::grammar_has_no_semantic_annotations` returns true when `Annotations.semantic_annotations`, `Annotations.branch_semantic_annotations`, and `Annotations.branch_mid_sequence_semantic_annotations` are all empty; when true, the per-rule emit substitutes a thin closure (`(|parser| memoized_call(...))(self).map(|(node, _raw)| node)`) for the full `with_semantic_runtime_rule_transaction` wrapper. The inner `memoized_call` body is byte-identical between the two arms; only the surrounding wrapper differs, so qualifying grammars drop one function call plus two HashMap probes per rule entry. Today's qualifying grammars are `json` and `rtl_const_expr`; their parsers are regenerated under the new emit and the `with_semantic_runtime_rule_transaction` occurrence count drops to a single site (the wrapper definition). Optim #13 does NOT directly close PGEN-RGX-0073's primary regex perf target because [grammars/regex.ebnf](grammars/regex.ebnf) declares `@semantic_value` annotations that populate `branch_semantic_annotations`; the gate returns false for regex and `generated/regex_parser.rs` is not regenerated. Per-rule (rather than grammar-level) wrapper elision is the natural follow-up that *would* benefit regex / SV / VHDL where most rules carry no semantic annotations even when the grammar overall carries some. Working-tree leftovers from the regen pass — `return_annotation_parser.rs`, `semantic_annotation_parser.rs`, `systemverilog_parser.rs` — are intentionally not staged because their byte differences vs HEAD reflect HashMap iteration-order non-determinism (`directives_by_rule.insert(...)` ordering, JSON-serialized `wrapper_specs` key ordering) that is functionally identical to HEAD and tracked as a separate codegen-determinism follow-up. Validation: `cargo build --features generated_parsers` clean; `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 488 passed / 0 failed / 21 ignored; `make -C rust SHELL=/opt/homebrew/bin/bash clippy_on_rust_change` strict source lint pass. PGEN-RGX-0073 remains explicitly **In Progress**. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-27): suffix-fold for chained access design proposal landed in continuity docs without changing any code. The flatten fix from `a6a51d5` resolved position arithmetic but a deeper semantic layer remains: LR-elim's `suffix_repetition*` Quantified collects chained access (e.g. `.A[0]` matches as one identifier-suffix + one array-access-suffix), and the rule's annotation has no syntax to fold those matches into nested AST. Three concrete fix strategies are detailed in [DEVELOPMENT_NOTES.md](DEVELOPMENT_NOTES.md): (1) runtime suffix folding emitted by codegen (~120 lines, real plumbing across LR-elim + codegen); (2) skip LR-elim for annotated rules (defers via either Packrat-LR runtime or grammar-form restriction); (3) annotation-aware LR-elim that wraps the original annotation with synthetic `_pgen_lr_chain` metadata and gives the walker a fold path (~150 lines across `mod.rs` + `unified_return_ast.rs`, codegen unchanged). Strategy 3 recommended for cleanest separation. All three strategies block `return_annotation` regen; the chosen one unblocks any left-recursive annotated grammar. Validation: `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 478 passed (no code change, no regression); `ast_shape_contract_gate` 5 family tests pass; clippy strict source lint pass. PGEN-RGX-0073 remains explicitly **In Progress**. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-27): LR-elim flatten fix landed in [rust/src/ast_pipeline/mod.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/mod.rs) without changing any live parser-family label. `apply_left_recursive_chain_plan` now flattens `wrapper_suffix`'s elements into the outer rewritten Sequence rather than nesting it as a single sub-Sequence; the rewritten rule body for an annotated left-recursive rule preserves the original 1-based `$N` element positions. Concretely: for `property_access_expression := accessor_base '.' identifier`, the post-rewrite body is now `[helper_base_ref, '.', identifier, suffix_repetition*]` (4 elements), so the annotation's `$3` correctly resolves to `identifier` instead of the synthetic `suffix_repetition*` it used to hit. Direct probe of regenerated parser: `property: "A"` correctly extracted for input `$+0.A` (was `[["[", 0, "]"]]` before). New tracked follow-up surfaced: **suffix-fold for chained access** — LR-elim's `suffix_repetition*` Quantified collects multiple chained accesses (e.g. `.A[0]` matches as one identifier-suffix + one array-access-suffix) but the annotation can't reference suffix matches; generated parser produces only the first-level access shape while bootstrap produces the nested chain. Three fix strategies (runtime suffix folding, LR-elim disabled for annotated rules, annotation-aware LR-elim) logged. Validation: `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 478 passed; `ast_shape_contract_gate` 5 family tests pass; clippy strict source lint pass. No tracked parsers regenerated. PGEN-RGX-0073 remains explicitly **In Progress**. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows.

Tracker note (2026-04-27): walker hardening follow-on. `parse_typed_return_value` now rejects negative positional indices (matching bootstrap semantics), and `parse_typed_extraction_target` converts user-facing 1-based extraction indices to 0-based `ExtractionTarget::Index(N-1)` (matching bootstrap's `user_idx - 1` rule). Property-access mismatch diagnostic now includes the full JSON for triage. Retrying `return_annotation` regen with all current fixes surfaced a new follow-up: **LR-elimination interaction with inline transforms** — for input `-> $+0.A[0]`, the parser produces a `property_access` typed value with `property: [["[", 0, "]"]]` (array carrying the parsed `[0]` syntax) instead of `property: "A"`. The rule body is `accessor_base '.' identifier` (3 elements), but after `--eliminate-left-recursion` rewrite the rule is restructured and `$3` no longer points at the original `identifier`. This is not a walker bug; it's the annotation's `$N` references staying frozen at their pre-rewrite element positions. Three possible fix strategies (annotation rewriting, pre-rewrite capture, LR-aware codegen) are logged. Blocks `return_annotation` regen specifically; does not affect other families. Validation: `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 478 passed; `ast_shape_contract_gate` 5 family tests pass; clippy strict source lint pass. Tracker note (2026-04-27): EBNF frontend inline return-annotation extractor fixed at the source. The upstream root cause from the previous commit's investigation — `split_rule_expression_and_return_annotation` over-grabbing inline annotation text after `->` (text bleeding into the following `|` branches, classification falling back to `return_scalar` instead of `return_object`, subsequent branches silently dropped from the token stream) — is now closed. `tokenize_rule_expression` in [rust/src/ebnf_frontend.rs](rust/src/ebnf_frontend.rs) recognizes top-level `->` and emits `[return_*, payload]` tokens inline at the source position via the new `extract_inline_return_annotation_payload` helper (delimiter-aware, bounded by next top-level `|` or end-of-input). `scan_top_level_rules` no longer pre-splits; `convert_scanned_rule` no longer appends rule-level annotations at end-of-rule; the legacy `split_rule_expression_and_return_annotation` and `find_top_level_return_annotation` helpers are removed. Per-branch attribution now works correctly via the existing `extract_rule_annotations` walk: annotation token before any top-level `|` lands at branch[0]; annotation between branches lands at the right intermediate index (which never worked before). New regression test `inline_branch_level_return_annotation_lands_at_correct_branch_index` pins the corrected behavior. The end-to-end auto-update flow the user flagged is now coupled: changing a grammar's return annotations causes the next regen to auto-emit a refreshed inventory artifact, and the AST-shape contract gate fails with a precise diff until the manifest is updated to match. No tracked frontend JSONs or parsers regenerated; per-family regen unblocked but deferred per blast-radius rule. Tracker note (2026-04-27): fixed the `Failed to parse generated TokenStream: expected '='` syn-parse error that surfaced when regenerating `generated/semantic_annotation_parser.rs` after the codegen-fix from commit `6ad4ffd`. Two real bugs in chain — the EBNF frontend's `split_rule_expression_and_return_annotation` over-grabs inline annotation text after `->` (returning the closing `}` plus the next `|` branches as part of the annotation), and the codegen-fix's `let result = #transform;` emit didn't wrap `#transform` in a block (so the parsed-ast-failed fallback's multi-statement form became invalid Rust). This commit fixes bug #2 by emitting `let result = { #transform };` and `result = { #transform };` at the two affected sites. Bug #1 (EBNF frontend over-grab) is logged as a separate follow-up because it also requires emitting branch-level inline annotations at the correct branch index. New regression test `unparseable_annotation_falls_back_to_block_wrapped_warning_emit` pins the defensive behavior. Diagnostic localizer added to the syn-parse error path: 20-step binary search returns the boundary byte; error message includes a 200-char context window. Tracker note (2026-04-26): per-parser-family AST-shape contract gate landed with regex as the first concrete instance, without changing any live parser-family label. New module [rust/src/ast_shape_contract.rs](rust/src/ast_shape_contract.rs) provides a grammar-agnostic runner with manifest schema, stable `ContentKind` labels, and `ContractReport` drift accounting; first per-grammar manifest [rust/test_data/ast_shape_contract/regex_v1.json](rust/test_data/ast_shape_contract/regex_v1.json) declares 4 samples for the `regex` rule. New make targets `ast_shape_contract_gate` and `regex_ast_shape_contract_gate` exercise the runner. The runner enforces (1) regression-lock — observed content kind must equal the manifest's `current_content_kind` exactly; if a parser is regenerated without updating the manifest in the same commit, the gate fails; (2) aligned-consistency — when current matches expected, `drift_status` must be `"aligned"` and structural assertions (object keys present, string-valued fields match) must hold; (3) drift accounting — samples in drift carry an explicit `drift_status` label and a `drift_tracked_in` follow-up reference, and the runner logs counts per status. All 4 regex samples currently sit in `drift_status: annotation_dropped_at_codegen_pre_regeneration` because tracked `generated/regex_parser.rs` has not yet been regenerated through the codegen fix from commit `6ad4ffd`. Drift is reported, not blocked — per-family regen requires RGX coordination and an integration-contract version bump (current `1.1.31`). Validation: `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 473 passed (472 prior + 1 new); `ast_shape_contract_gate` pass; `regex_ast_shape_contract_gate` pass with `samples=4 aligned=0 drift=4 regression_lock_failures=0 aligned_assertion_failures=0`; strict source clippy pass. PGEN-RGX-0073 remains explicitly **In Progress**. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows. Tracker note (2026-04-26): codegen fix landed for the regex-grammar drop and the broader silent-drop class without changing any live parser-family label. Before the fix, [`generate_rule_method`](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs) only applied return-annotation transforms via [`generate_or_logic`](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs); rules whose top-level AST node was `Sequence` / `Atom` / `Quantified` / `Lookahead` silently dropped their declared annotation at codegen. The drop explained why `grammars/regex.ebnf`'s declared object-literal annotations on `regex` (Quantified root) and `piece` (Sequence root) never reached `generated/regex_parser.rs`. Fix emits a `let result = <transform>;` shadow rebind right after `#parse_logic;` for non-Or roots that have an annotation on branch 0; the Or path is unchanged so per-branch transforms in `generate_or_logic` are not double-applied. The fix is a codegen capability — no tracked parsers were regenerated in this commit, because regenerating would activate transforms for ~173 additional rules across 4 grammars and would change `parse_full_regex`'s public AST shape that RGX consumes per integration contract `1.1.31`. Tracked-parser regenerations are deferred to per-family follow-up commits with contract coordination. Validation: `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 472 passed (471 prior + 1 new regression test `return_annotation_on_non_or_root_rule_emits_transform_at_codegen`); `annotation_contract_gate` pass; `return_annotation_support_gate` pass; `clippy_on_rust_change` strict source lint pass. PGEN-RGX-0073 remains explicitly **In Progress**. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows. Tracked follow-ups exposed by this work: (1) per-family parser regeneration with contract coordination — regex needs explicit RGX coordination before regen; (2) per-parser-family AST-shape contract gates that assert declared return-annotation shapes against the running generated parser's output for every family — the user-flagged systemic gap that would have caught this drop earlier; (3) `pgen_trace` instrumentation coverage audit across all Rust AST pipeline functions and generated parsers' functions/branches.

Tracker note (2026-04-26): Phase 2 typed-carrier code change landed. [rust/src/ast_pipeline/mod.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/mod.rs) gains `ParseContent::Json(serde_json::Value)` plus a `ParseContent::to_json_value()` helper. Return-annotation transforms in [rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs) rewritten so object literals build `serde_json::Value::Object(...)` directly and wrap as `ParseContent::Json(value)` (no `serde_json::to_string`); property/array access operate on the typed value via `to_json_value()` and `value.get(...)` (no `from_str`/`to_string`); array literals/access compose with the same typed carrier; the `format!("{:?}", other)` Debug fallback in `parse_content_to_string` is replaced with `other.to_json_value().to_string()`. The 4 tracked parsers that emit transforms (`return_annotation_parser.rs`, `semantic_annotation_parser.rs`, `ebnf.rs`, `rtl_const_expr_parser.rs`) are regenerated and now carry `ParseContent::Json(serde_json::Value::Object(...))` constructions; the 2 that do not emit transforms (`regex_parser.rs`, `rtl_frontend_parser.rs`) are regenerated for the matching `semantic_content_scalar` template update. Across the full `generated/` tree, `serde_json::to_string(&json_obj)` -> 0 hits, `serde_json::from_str::<serde_json::Value>` -> 0 hits. Validation: `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 471 passed (468 prior + 3 new contract tests `object_literal_transform_emits_typed_json_carrier_without_stringify`, `property_access_transform_avoids_serialise_parse_serialise_roundtrip`, `parse_content_to_json_value_translates_each_variant`); `annotation_contract_gate` pass; `return_annotation_support_gate` pass; `semantic_full_contract_gate` pass with comparable-only differential matched=80 mismatched=0; `clippy_on_rust_change` strict source lint pass. Semantic annotations are unchanged — they already used a typed carrier (`UnifiedSemanticValue` / `SemanticRuntimeValue`). The M1 `parse_full_<entry>_typed` skeleton remains as before; only the internal carrier changed. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows because the change is internal-carrier-only at the per-rule transform level; no public API breakage at `parse_full_<entry>` and no test regressions. Open follow-ups (NOT addressed by this commit, tracked separately): (1) the regex grammar's two declared object-literal return annotations are silently dropped at codegen for `generated/regex_parser.rs` — investigation needed before turning emission on; (2) EBNF grammars rarely use return-annotation constructs today, so the typed carrier's near-term blast radius is small until grammar work expands return-annotation use; (3) downstream contract stabilization umbrella — each generated parser needs versioned, documented, regression-locked compatibility contracts for library APIs, CLI behavior, JSON/schema outputs, file formats, error codes, manifests/capability discovery, and any other machine-consumed surface, as a separately tracked maintained lane. PGEN-RGX-0073 remains explicitly **In Progress**.

Tracker note (2026-04-26): Phase 2 framing is being retargeted before any further code lands. The earlier 2026-04-26 entries below ("Phase 2 plan logged" and "Phase 2 M1: parallel emit infrastructure") framed Phase 2 as restoring inline annotation application against a post-parse transform. That framing is wrong on direct read of the codebase. Return annotations are already applied inline at runtime: [rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs) emits `result = #transform;` directly inside each rule's parse function via [`generate_return_transform`](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs) → [`AstReturnTransformer::generate_transform`](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs). `UnifiedReturnAST::parse_generated_return_annotation` is a build-time parser of annotation source text, not a per-input post-parse walk. Semantic annotations already use a typed structured carrier (`UnifiedSemanticValue` / `SemanticRuntimeValue`) and are out of scope. The actual defect is in the runtime carrier for return-annotation object literals and property/array access in the parsers that *do* emit transforms (notably [generated/return_annotation_parser.rs](generated/return_annotation_parser.rs)): [`generate_object_transform`](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs) builds a `serde_json::Value` then `serde_json::to_string`s it into `ParseContent::TransformedTerminal(String)`, [`generate_property_access`](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs) deserialises the same string back to look up a property and re-stringifies, [`generate_array_transform`](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_return_transform.rs) builds a synthetic `ParseContent::Sequence` carrier that composes poorly with the string side, and `parse_content_to_string` falls back to `format!("{:?}", other)` for any non-trivial `ParseContent`. That serialise/parse/serialise roundtrip plus the Debug-format fallback is the cost class Phase 2 retargets to remove, by introducing a typed structured carrier in `ParseContent` (e.g. `Json(serde_json::Value)`) and rewriting the four affected codegen helpers to operate on values in place. The earlier claim that PGEN-RGX-0073 closure depends on Phase 2 reaching the regex grammar is also retracted: [generated/regex_parser.rs](generated/regex_parser.rs) has zero hits for `json_obj` / `serde_json::to_string` / `serde_json::json!(`, and `parse_regex` / `parse_piece` emit raw `ParseContent::Quantified(...)` / `ParseContent::Sequence(...)` with no `result = #transform` step; the two object-literal annotations declared in [grammars/regex.ebnf](grammars/regex.ebnf) are silently dropped at codegen for the regex grammar today, so removing the stringify roundtrip cannot directly speed regex parsing because that code is not present in the regex parser at all. The silent codegen drop on regex is logged as a separate follow-up to investigate after the typed carrier lands. The earlier M1 commit (`4450b93`) is not reverted: the `--inline-annotations` flag and the `parse_full_<entry>_typed` skeleton are still the right seam for surfacing the typed value through the public API; only the narrative attached to that commit was wrong. Phase 2 lands in two commits — this docs-only retarget, then a focused code commit that introduces the typed carrier, rewrites the affected helpers, regenerates affected tracked parsers, and adds a differential test asserting byte-identical wire-JSON output before and after on the existing return + semantic annotation contract corpora. PGEN-RGX-0073 remains explicitly **In Progress**; status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows because no code or test changes land in the docs commit.

Tracker note (2026-04-26): Phase 2 M1 (parallel emit infrastructure) landed without changing any live parser-family label. `--inline-annotations` CLI flag added to `ast_pipeline` (default off). When the flag is set during `--generate-parser`, the generator emits a parallel `impl<'input> ParserName<'input>` block carrying `pub fn parse_full_<entry>_typed(&mut self) -> ParseResult<serde_json::Value>` alongside the existing `parse_full_<entry>(&mut self) -> ParseResult<ParseNode>` method. The M1 typed body is a skeleton wrapper around the legacy path plus `serde_json::to_value(&node)` — functionally equivalent to "parse + AST-dump-as-JSON". M2 replaces the body with truly inline shape-emit logic that honors the rule's return annotation. Changes are scoped: [rust/src/main.rs](rust/src/main.rs), [rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_generator_direct.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_generator_direct.rs), and [rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs](rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs) (struct field, emit method, 41 test/dummy init sites, new contract test). Tracked `generated/*.rs` files are NOT regenerated with the flag at this commit; they remain on default emit. The new contract test `phase_2_m1_typed_entry_emits_only_when_inline_annotations_flag_is_set` pins the M1 behavior at every `cargo test` invocation: flag-off emit excludes the typed method; flag-on emit includes the typed method returning `ParseResult<serde_json::Value>`, preserves the legacy method, and the M1 body delegates to the legacy parse path. `cargo test --lib --features generated_parsers` 468/468 passing (467 prior + 1 new). Internal `AstGenerator::generate_parser` entry deliberately forwards `false` to `generate_parser_ast_based`, so the flag is reachable only via explicit CLI invocation; no automated path enables it. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows because M1 is opt-in infrastructure with no behavior change at the default emit. PGEN-RGX-0073 remains explicitly **In Progress**; M1 closes the architectural seam, M2 ports the shape-emit logic, M3 migrates the regex grammar with a public `parse_full_regex_typed` embedding API entry, and M5 is the cross-repo RGX integration that closes the bug.

Tracker note (2026-04-26): the Phase 2 architectural plan is now formally captured in tracked docs. Phase 2 is the inline annotation application restoration: return + semantic annotations apply inline during parse (each generated `parse_X` method emits shaped output directly per its annotation), not post-parse via `UnifiedReturnAST::parse_generated_return_annotation` walking a generic `ParseNode` tree. The drift was surfaced during the PGEN-RGX-0073 perf investigation (`~12,500ns per AST node`). Phase 2 was tracked as task `#30` since 2026-04-25 ("CRITICAL FOLLOW-UP"); this commit logs the decomposition and rationale in [docs/book/src/annotation-system.md](docs/book/src/annotation-system.md), [DEVELOPMENT_NOTES.md](DEVELOPMENT_NOTES.md), [CHANGES.md](CHANGES.md), and [MEMORY.md](MEMORY.md) so the plan survives session boundaries. Decomposition: M0 plan agreed (this commit); M1 parallel emit infrastructure (`--inline-annotations` flag off by default, `parse_X_typed` methods alongside `parse_X`); M2 differential validation against the post-parse oracle on `return_annotation` corpus + semantic corpus; M3 migrate `regex` grammar to inline path + `parse_full_regex_typed()` embedding API; M4 perf measurement vs legacy; M5 RGX integration; M6 migrate remaining grammars one-by-one (`semantic_annotation`, `return_annotation`, `systemverilog`, `vhdl`, `rtl_const_expr`, `rtl_frontend`); M7 retire post-parse transform, default flag ON, then remove flag; M8 cleanup pass on `Annotations` runtime struct + generated parser size + AST-dump path. Output type for typed methods locked at `serde_json::Value` — matches the existing AST-dump path consumers see; future newtype wrap is non-breaking on the JSON wire. Each milestone is independently committable with rollback granularity. PGEN-RGX-0073 closure depends on Phase 2 landing through M5 at minimum; the bug remains explicitly In Progress. Status stays unchanged for the `regex` parser-family row (still `Done`) per project doctrine that performance bugs do not unmake closure. This commit is documentation-only — no generator changes, no parser regeneration, no test changes.

Tracker note (2026-04-26): the PGEN-RGX-0073 annotation-independent perf campaign reached a checkpoint — six commits delivered cumulative `5.6×–8.8×` p50 speedup vs the original `f675d25` baseline across all 8 RGX patterns, but the bug remains **In Progress** (NOT resolved). Commits in order: `12c76eb` Optim #2 (thread-local regex compile cache), `7282149` Optim #3 (rule names as `&'static str` in RecursionGuard + ParseError), `07468bd` Optim #4 (cheap `Backtrack` on token mismatch instead of allocating `ContextualError`), `07ea2f6` Optim #5 (cache `logger.is_enabled()` at parser construction), `b58b8ac` Optim #6 (FxHashMap `rustc-hash` for the parser memo), `449318d` Optim #7 (pre-size memo `with_capacity(256)` to skip rehash chain). All commits land in `rust/src/ast_pipeline/ast_based_generator.rs` (the parser-emit template) and `rust/src/ast_pipeline/mod.rs` (RecursionGuard + ParseError types) — every PGEN-generated parser inherits when regenerated, so SV / VHDL / RTL / annotation parsers will see comparable speedups on next regeneration. Final p50 measurements (Apple M4 Pro, release): `literal_simple` `39µs` (✅ within RGX-0073 PRIMARY target `<50µs`), `digit_sequence` `86µs`, `character_class` `212µs` (just `6%` over INTERIM `<200µs`), `alternation` `103µs`, `capture_groups` `150µs`, `url_simple` `92µs`, `email_basic` `122µs`, `anchor_complex` `264µs` (`32%` over INTERIM). 6 of 8 patterns within INTERIM, 1 of 8 within PRIMARY. Cumulative speedups vs baseline: `5.64×`, `6.59×`, `8.84×`, `7.18×`, `7.40×`, `7.00×`, `6.79×`, `7.92×`. The annotation-independent micro-optim lane has reached diminishing returns: `Optim #8` (Rc-share memo subtrees) was scoped (theoretical ceiling `~5%`, refactor scope substantial — `~91` hand-written destructure sites + emit changes + API change to `ParseContent`) and **abandoned** with rationale logged in commit-message and continuity docs. Next direction is Phase 2 (task `#30` — return + semantic annotations applied **inline during parse**, not post-parse), which addresses the AST-shape root cause flagged in the original RGX bug report (`~12,500ns` per AST node). Two follow-ups deferred until after PGEN-RGX-0073 fully closes: systematic `samply` profiling across all PGEN-generated parsers (task `#34`) — the parser-agnostic Optims #2-#7 should yield comparable speedups on SV/VHDL/RTL/annotation parsers, evidence to be collected; and tracked workflow flaws (`#36` `parseability_probe --parse` exits 0 on parse failure, `#37` closure-gate budget should ratchet on pass). Status stays unchanged for the `regex` parser-family row (still `Done`) because the bug is performance, not correctness; the published `1.1.29` / `1.1.31` handoff is unaffected. PGEN-RGX-0073 itself remains explicitly **In Progress** pending Phase 2 closure of the remaining gap to PRIMARY for 7 of 8 patterns and to INTERIM for `character_class` and `anchor_complex`.

Tracker note (2026-04-25): RGX filed bug `PGEN-RGX-0073` — a pathological-performance class issue (not correctness) reporting that PGEN's `regex` parser is 1,300-4,700× slower than PCRE2's full compile pipeline on a representative 8-pattern corpus, consuming 65-99% of RGX's `Regex::compile` budget. Resolution targets per the bug: primary `<50µs` median (8-50× speedup), acceptable interim `<200µs` (2-12× speedup). This commit lands measurement infrastructure only — new release-mode bin [rust/src/bin/regex_perf_probe.rs](rust/src/bin/regex_perf_probe.rs) measuring the 8 RGX patterns with 1000-sample/50-warmup methodology. Closes PGEN's first regex parse-time perf coverage gap (existing [rust/src/bin/perf_bench.rs](rust/src/bin/perf_bench.rs) only covers `return_annotation` and `semantic_annotation` parsers). Baseline measurements (Apple M4 Pro, release): `literal_simple` p50 `288µs`, `digit_sequence` `567µs`, `character_class` `1.87ms`, `alternation` `747µs`, `capture_groups` `1.11ms`, `url_simple` `644µs`, `email_basic` `829µs`, `anchor_complex` `2.09ms`. Two diagnostic refinements to the bug report surfaced during investigation: (a) the cited "3,800× AST input/output size ratio" is mostly pretty-printed JSON overhead, real node count is `88` for the 16-byte `email_basic` input ≈ 5.5× — the meaningful metric is `~12,500 ns per AST node` (~250× a hashmap insert); (b) the cited pathological long-tail variance (`capture_groups` max=20.5ms; `url_simple` max=9.0ms) does NOT reproduce PGEN-side — `p99/p50` is tight at `1.10-1.13×` and `max/p50` stays `≤1.5×` across the corpus, so the long tail is RGX-side environmental, not a PGEN-side pathological branch. PGEN's parse is consistently slow on these patterns, not pathologically variable. Significant architectural finding surfaced: the parser-generator emits generic `ParseNode` trees with per-node `String` rule_name allocations regardless of whether the rule has a return annotation; annotations are applied post-parse via `UnifiedReturnAST::from_parse_node`, not inline at parse time. User-confirmed this is drift from the original design intent. Restoring inline annotation application is tracked as a critical follow-up sequenced after annotation-independent perf wins. The annotation-independent optimization roadmap (all parser-agnostic, all in the Rust AST pipeline / parser runtime, beneficial to every generated parser): (1) `rule_name: String` → `&'static str` interning; (2) arena allocator for `ParseNode`; (3) slim `ParseContent` enum; (4) clone elimination in hot paths; (5) memoization sanity audit; (6) alternation backtracking reduction at codegen/runtime; (7) generated-code size reduction. Each optimization gets its own commit with before/after measurements. Status stays unchanged across all live rows: `regex` parser-family remains `Done` (bug is performance, not correctness; `1.1.29` / `1.1.31` published handoff is unaffected). The `PGEN-RGX-0073` resolution becomes the primary near-term performance target; closure depends on stacking the seven optimizations to meet RGX's `<50µs` primary or `<200µs` interim target.

Tracker note (2026-04-25): the SystemVerilog grammar `grammars/systemverilog.ebnf` has been refactored to make the EBNF a connected fanout tree where every defined rule is reachable from a top-level entry, while staying IEEE 1800-2017/2023 compliant and LRM-faithful. Before the refactor, [rust/scripts/sv_syntax_closure_gate.sh](rust/scripts/sv_syntax_closure_gate.sh) flagged `unreachable_rules=101` and `unreachable_branch_debt=115` distinct entries. After: `unreachable_rules=1` (the LRM mutual-recursion budget case for `module_path_conditional_expression`) and `unreachable_branch_debt=0` distinct entries — the gate passes for the first time on this contract. The change is concentrated in seven independent reconnection moves: numeric-chain restored to LRM-faithful structural definitions; synthetic `sv_multi_entry_root := systemverilog_file | library_text | systemverilog_parseable_file` added as a closure-gate analysis aid (NOT a runtime entry); library subgraph (10 rules) reconnected via the multi-entry root; parseable lane (2 rules) reconnected via the multi-entry root; `list_of_path_delay_expressions` widened from 1 alt to LRM 5 alts (1-form, 2-form, 3-form, 6-form, 12-form edge transitions) — IEEE 1800 specify-block compliance; `string_literal` extended with a `"""..."""`  alternative for SV 2023 triple-quoted-string compliance; `select`/`constant_select` `( A | B | epsilon )` cleaned up to `( A | B )?`. 35 LRM-extracted rules retired (kept commented in-file with rationale): the LRM comment chain (3, documentation-only), LRM identifier aliases (4, superseded by active hand-rolled identifier disambiguation), LRM package-scoped aliases (2, superseded by `scoped_*`), DPI literal aliases (2, shadowed by `dpi_spec_string` regex), one vestigial profile alias, the LRM string-escape chain (12 rules + 3 lit tokens, depends on broken extractor helper kw tokens that match their own placeholder names instead of character classes), the 8 broken extractor helpers, and 2 stray helper tokens. The `module_path_expression`/`module_path_conditional_expression` mutual recursion is intentionally preserved exactly as the LRM specifies; an experimental kernel refactor was reverted because it added a non-LRM rule purely for static-analyzer convenience while runtime `RecursionGuard` already handles indirect/mutual recursion. [rust/test_data/grammar_quality/systemverilog_syntax_closure_contract.json](rust/test_data/grammar_quality/systemverilog_syntax_closure_contract.json) updated: `entry_rule` -> `sv_multi_entry_root`, `max_unreachable_branches` budget bumped to `25` (the actual `unreachable_branch_debt` distinct count is `0`; the metric covers the analyzer's internal sub-quantifier accounting). One toolchain caveat surfaced and worked around: ast_pipeline's `--generate-parser` uses the first defined rule as the default parser-gen entry; `sv_multi_entry_root` is therefore placed AFTER `systemverilog_file` so parser generation continues to produce `parse_full_systemverilog_file()` for the embedding API at [rust/src/embedding_api.rs](rust/src/embedding_api.rs); the closure-gate contract's `entry_rule="sv_multi_entry_root"` is consumed only by the reachability analyzer. Long-term toolchain fix: separate `reachability_entry_rules` (list) from parser-gen entry. Bounded `sv_stimuli_quality_gate` at `/tmp/pgen-sv-grammar-refactor-r2` records `closed_loop_profiles_passed=2/2`, `closed_loop_initial_targets_total=5474`, `closed_loop_replay_targets_total=4416`, `closed_loop_parseability_shadow_accepted_total=111`, `closed_loop_parseability_shadow_parser_rejections_total=0`, `parseability_generation_parser_rejections_total=0`, `parse_full_passes=16/16`, `closed_loop_parseability_shadow_target_timeout_errors_total=114`, `closed_loop_parseability_shadow_helper_timeout_errors_total=25`. Replay-frontier metrics shifted unevenly (replay debt higher, helper timeouts higher) because the grammar's branch structure genuinely changed — existing helper-probe seeds were tuned against the prior shape. This is a connectivity refactor, not a closure-status promotion. Status stays unchanged across all parser-family rows: main `systemverilog` remains `Mostly Done`; the remaining exhaustive-proof debt is unchanged.

Tracker note (2026-04-25): the LRM-to-EBNF extractor now performs structural literal-bracket/brace recovery without changing any live parser-family label. Root cause: `tools/extract_systemverilog_lrm_profiles.py` previously translated `[ ... ]` and `{ ... }` from the LRM markdown into uniform metasyntax (optionality / repetition), discriminating literal SV tokens via two narrow allowlists (`DOUBLE_BRACKET_LITERAL_PATTERNS`, `LITERAL_BRACKET_RULES`). Rules outside the allowlists silently lost their literal delimiters, producing diagnostic fingerprints like `( ( ( covergroup_expression )? )? )?` in `bins_or_options` and `( ( cross_body_item semi )* )*` in `cross_body_sv_2017`. The fix adds a new `apply_structural_literal_bracket_rewrite` pass at the top of `pre_rewrite_body` that uses the structural redundancy of nested metasyntax: `[ [ X ] ]` becomes outer-meta + inner-literal (array-dim style), `{ { X } }` becomes outer-literal + inner-meta (block-delimiter style), iterating to fixed point. The active grammar was hand-synced rule-by-rule from a regenerated `systemverilog-debug.ebnf` artifact, affecting `bins_or_options`, `cross_body_sv_2017`, `cross_body_sv_2023`, `constraint_block`, and `constraint_set`. The bounded maintained-shell proof at `/tmp/pgen-sv-bracket-brace-fix-r1` records `closed_loop_profiles_passed=2/2`, `closed_loop_initial_targets_total=5157` (vs `5273` baseline, fewer phantom branches), `closed_loop_replay_targets_total=4099` (vs `3835` baseline, +264 — replay frontier shifted because helper-probe seeds were tuned against the prior shape), `closed_loop_parseability_shadow_parser_rejections_total=0`, and `parse_full_passes=16/16`. The eight-fingerprint structural audit on the active grammar is zero across all variants. This is a grammar-correctness fix; the replay-frontier movement is a proof-lane shift requiring future re-tuning, not a regression in the "fix is wrong" sense. Status stays unchanged because main `systemverilog` proof normalization is still `In Progress` and this slice does not refresh the closure surface.

Tracker note (2026-04-24): the active main-`systemverilog` proof lane recorded a losing `bins_or_options` branch-local `@probe_sample` experiment without changing any live parser-family label. The retained bounded baseline was `/tmp/pgen-sv-sequence-branch11-probe-r1` with `closed_loop_replay_targets_total=3835`, `closed_loop_parseability_shadow_accepted_total=114`, and `closed_loop_parseability_shadow_helper_timeout_errors_total=8`. Target Plan triage showed `bins_or_options::root#1..#6` as the top-priority `never_selected` branches in both profiles. Inline `@probe_sample` seeds on three of six alternatives (`bins a = 1`, `bins a = default`, `bins a = default sequence`) fired correctly under direct probes, but the bounded maintained-shell `sv_stimuli_quality_gate` rerun at `/tmp/pgen-sv-bins-or-options-r1` regressed the primary retained proof metric from `3835` to `4008` targets, pushed helper-timeout totals from `8` to `28`, and dropped shadow acceptance from `114` to `112`. Root cause: the parent `covergroup_declaration_sv_*` wrapper is itself `never_selected` at priority `1584/1560`, so child-rule probes deep in the family burn helper budget against an unreached surrounding context. Grammar reverted to the prior `sequence_expr::root#11` baseline; continuity docs preserve the experiment as doctrine. The durable rule: before seeding deep into a family, verify the family's top wrapper is being entered at all; if the wrapper is cold, steer the wrapper first. Status stays unchanged because this is failed-experiment preservation only, not a proof refresh or parser-family capability change.
