Tracker note (2026-04-09): the fourth deferred stimuli-platform upgrade is now implemented without changing any live label. Corpus export / promotion groundwork is landed behind `--stimuli-corpus-json`, with a deliberately bounded first slice that emits deterministic machine-readable corpus bundles for direct generation, generated stimuli modules, and minimized coverage-guided fuzz output. The current bundle surface preserves replay-relevant generation config, emitted samples, coverage, parseability summary/counterexamples when available, and minimized fuzz promotion metadata including source seed plus new rule/branch hits and normalized coverage tokens. The shared cross-family validation rule is again exercised through real bounded bundle exports on `regex`, `vhdl`, and `systemverilog`, while the module-surface export also preserves the deterministic default-seed reality (`requested_seed=null`, `effective_seed=1`) when `--seed` is omitted. This means the first four preserved stimuli backlog items are now landed; the next deferred stimuli-platform step is `smarter shrinkers`. No parser-family row changed because this is shared stimuli-platform strengthening rather than a family-specific closure promotion.
Tracker note (2026-04-09): the third deferred stimuli-platform upgrade is now implemented without changing any live label. Stronger near-valid negative generation is landed behind `--stimuli-negative-profile`, with the initial deliberately bounded non-baseline profile:
- `near_valid_local`
The current shipped negative slice prefers deterministic local structural corruption rather than blunt truncation-only shaping. The bounded candidate set currently focuses on closing-delimiter removal/mismatch, duplicated or trailing separators, and small interior local deletions, with deterministic negative-marker fallback retained when no stronger local corruption candidate exists. The shared cross-family validation rule is again exercised through real bounded replays on `regex`, `vhdl`, and `systemverilog`. All three families generated successfully in both baseline and near-valid-negative modes, and all three produced different outputs versus baseline. This means the first three preserved stimuli backlog items are now landed; the next deferred stimuli-platform step is `corpus export/promotion`. No parser-family row changed because this is shared stimuli-platform strengthening rather than a family-specific closure promotion.
Tracker note (2026-04-09): the second deferred stimuli-platform upgrade is now implemented without changing any live label. Constrained-random steering is landed behind `--stimuli-constraint-profile`, with the initial deliberately bounded profile set:
- `rare_branch_biased`
- `deep_nesting_biased`
The current shipped steering slice reuses the existing generator’s deterministic weighting / quantifier-choice seams rather than introducing a separate generator path, and the shared cross-family validation rule is again exercised through real bounded replays on `regex`, `vhdl`, and `systemverilog`. All three families generated successfully in both baseline and deep-nesting-steered modes, and all three produced different outputs versus baseline. This means the first two preserved stimuli backlog items are now landed; the next deferred stimuli-platform step is `stronger near-valid negative generation`. No parser-family row changed because this is shared stimuli-platform strengthening rather than a family-specific closure promotion.
Tracker note (2026-04-09): the first deferred stimuli-platform upgrade is now implemented without changing any live label. Grammar-aware mutation is landed behind `--stimuli-mutation-mode grammar_aware_local`, with the initial deliberately bounded scope of local OR-branch and quantifier-repeat perturbation over baseline recovery-mode generation. The cross-family validation rule is now exercised by real bounded replays on `regex`, `vhdl`, and `systemverilog`, and all three families generated successfully in both baseline and mutation modes with differing outputs. This means the stimuli backlog is no longer “all planned, nothing landed”: item `1` is now in place, and the next deferred stimuli-platform step is `constrained-random steering`. No parser-family row changed because this is shared stimuli-platform strengthening rather than a family-specific closure promotion.
Tracker note (2026-04-08): the current stimuli-generation implementation strategy is now explicitly preserved in [docs/reference/PGEN_STIMULI_MODULE_NORMATIVE_SPEC.md](docs/reference/PGEN_STIMULI_MODULE_NORMATIVE_SPEC.md) and the deferred execution order is now explicitly planned in [docs/reference/PGEN_SOTA_IMPLEMENTATION_ROADMAP.md](docs/reference/PGEN_SOTA_IMPLEMENTATION_ROADMAP.md), without changing any live label. The retained preferred upgrade order is: grammar-aware mutation, constrained-random steering, stronger near-valid negative generation, corpus export/promotion, and smarter shrinkers. Major generator upgrades should be replay-validated against at least `systemverilog`, `vhdl`, and `regex` so active families benefit while closed families act as regression sentinels. That policy is now executable through `make -C rust SHELL=/bin/bash stimuli_cross_family_platform_gate`, which reuses bounded real-family quality lanes instead of a synthetic toy harness. The retained local-runtime hygiene follow-up also landed: `sv_stimuli_quality_gate.sh` now builds `ast_pipeline` and `parseability_probe` together under the same generated-adapter environment instead of rebuilding them separately. The shared wrapper is now explicitly tuned for local replay: it forces `cargo_build_jobs=1` across the regex / VHDL / SystemVerilog slices, trims the bounded SV replay budget from `200` to `50`, and uses the bounded shared SV mode `sv_parseable_file` instead of the much heavier `sv_file` surface. That finally closes the local wrapper caveat: `make -C rust SHELL=/bin/bash stimuli_cross_family_platform_gate` is now locally green end to end, with regex and VHDL bounded slices passing and the bounded SV slice proving `closed_loop_initial_targets_total=53`, `closed_loop_replay_targets_total=21`, and full gate pass under `stimuli_mode=sv_parseable_file`. Tracker note (2026-04-08): regex handoff is now also published as downstream maintenance release `1.1.9` without changing the live label. This closes RGX feature request `PGEN-RGX-0015` by widening parenthesized subroutine-call forms to carry PCRE2 `10.47+` returned-capture grouplists, so both `(?1(1))` and `(?&callee(+1,<cap>,'alt'))` now transport through explicit AST rules `returned_capture_subroutine`, `subroutine_target`, `returned_capture_group_list`, and `returned_capture_group` instead of rejecting at byte `0`. The published regex manifest and direct AST-shape proof surface now retain both numeric and named returned-capture forms; regex status remains `Done` because this is a published syntax-widening maintenance release, not a change in the closure doctrine.

### Major Roadmap Phases

Phase completion tracks whether a roadmap phase delivered its stated contract. It does not automatically mean every parser family touched by those phases is equally mature; parser-family maturity is normalized separately below.

| Area | Status | Evidence | Left To Close |
|---|---|---|---|
| Phases A-R | Done | Roadmap phases `A` through `R` currently show only completed checklist items. | Nothing material inside the currently tracked phase checklists. |
| Phase S overall: RTLSyn parser stack minimum viable coverage | In Progress | `rtl_const_expr` and `rtl_frontend` are active executable crates with passing tests; `rtl_const_expr` now also has a tracked EBNF plus generated parser path, and `rtl_frontend` now also has a tracked bootstrap grammar plus generated parser artifacts/build-registry wiring with clean Rust-frontend verification, but the frontend still lacks parity/proof closure against the handwritten baseline and Liberty/SDC remain unstarted. | Close the retained `rtl_frontend` proof/parity gap and start the still-missing companion parser crates. |

Parser-family status note:
`make -C rust SHELL=/opt/homebrew/bin/bash sv_parser_family_status_gate` now computes the tracked `systemverilog` / `systemverilog_preprocessor` statuses directly from machine-checkable proof surfaces and fails if they drift from this file. The main `systemverilog` status now depends on `sv_syntax_closure_gate`, `sv_parser_aggregate_contract_gate`, `sv_semantic_scope_contract_gate`, and the retained `sv_formal_exhaustive_closure_gate` sidecar; the preprocessor status now also carries the explicit `sv_preprocessor_formal_exhaustive_closure_gate` seam inside the retained family-status sidecar itself, in addition to `sv_preprocessor_syntax_closure_gate`, `sv_preprocessor_aggregate_contract_gate`, and `sv_preprocessor_reachability_closure_gate`. `make -C rust SHELL=/opt/homebrew/bin/bash sv_parser_family_status_contract_gate` now validates the produced family-status sidecar itself for schema shape, tracker-alignment consistency, closure-count arithmetic, false-criteria accounting, and structured-blocker parity between `summary.json` and `summary.txt`, including the propagated SystemVerilog and SystemVerilog-preprocessor formal-closure proof fields. Tracker note (2026-04-06): regex handoff is now published as downstream maintenance release `1.1.7`. That release carries forward the `1.1.6` tagged embedded-code span fix and closes RGX issue `PGEN-RGX-0010`, which was an accepted-tree ambiguity in conditional recursion tests: ordered PEG choice let `name` shadow `recursion_condition` for forms such as `(?(R1)b|c)`. With `condition` now trying `recursion_condition` before `name`, both bare `R` and numeric `R1` forms transport correctly without changing regex AST schema version `1`.
Tracker note (2026-04-06): the upstream regex integration-contract surface is also now stronger on the oracle side. [regex_parser_integration_contract_v1.json](rust/test_data/grammar_quality/regex_parser_integration_contract_v1.json) and [regex_embedded_code_block_contract_v0.json](rust/test_data/grammar_quality/regex_embedded_code_block_contract_v0.json) can now declare `expected_rule_texts` in addition to `required_rule_names` / `forbidden_rule_names`, the generated-backend embedding tests replay those text expectations generically, and the dedicated embedded-code shell gate now checks extracted `code_lang` / `code_content` text directly. The retained protected seams now include `(?R)`, `\1`, `\g<1>`, `\o{101}`, tagged-code-block classification/content integrity, and the recursion-conditional distinction among `(?(R)a|b)`, `(?(R1)b|c)`, and `(?(R&word)a|b)`. This should remain the preferred first-line defense for accepted-tree transport regressions; broader stimuli randomness alone is not a sufficient oracle for those cases.
Tracker note (2026-04-08): focused `rtl_frontend` parity debugging has now removed two real generated-parser false negatives without changing the live label. Second, module parameter headers no longer misparse untyped forms like `parameter DEPTH = 4` as typed declarations: the `rtl_frontend` grammar now uses explicit lookahead to require `( data_type identifier )` for typed parameter branches while preserving the untyped branch. Focused generated replays now stay green for the retained `always_ff`, parameterized unpacked-port, imported-enum typedef-port, and unpacked-struct-member-actual samples, while the malformed truncated-header negative still rejects. Tracker note (2026-04-07): regex handoff is now published as downstream maintenance release `1.1.8`. This release closes RGX issues `PGEN-RGX-0011`, `PGEN-RGX-0012`, and `PGEN-RGX-0013`: the grammar now accepts Unicode literal atoms and mixed ASCII/UTF-8 literal runs such as `🎉` and `café`; the generated parser recursion guard is now materially wider but still bounded (`512` instead of `100`); and the public regex host entrypoints now run the generated backend on a dedicated larger-stack worker thread so `50` nested capturing groups no longer trip the smaller test-thread stack. The retained oracle surface is wider too: the published regex integration-contract manifest now carries explicit success samples for `unicode_emoji_literal`, `unicode_accented_literal`, and `nested_capturing_groups_50`, and those samples are replayed both by manifest-driven AST-shape tests and by direct `parseability_probe` repros against the RGX artifact inputs.

This does not change any live status row; it just keeps the tracked workflow export path honest and resume-friendly.
Tracker note (2026-04-06): regex handoff is now published as downstream maintenance release `1.1.4`. That release closes RGX issue `PGEN-RGX-0007` by widening `subroutine_ref` so numeric angle forms such as `\g<1>` transport as `backreference` plus `subroutine_ref` / `signed_digits` instead of degrading into `simple_escape("g")` plus literal `<`, `1`, `>` without changing regex AST schema version `1`.
Tracker note (2026-04-05): regex handoff is now published as downstream maintenance release `1.1.3`. That release closes RGX issue `PGEN-RGX-0006` by modeling braced octal escapes and hardening brace-style escape skipping in the compile validator, so `\o{101}` now transports as a real octal escape instead of `simple_escape` plus counted quantifier without changing regex AST schema version `1`.
Tracker note (2026-04-01): regex handoff is now published as downstream maintenance release `1.1.2`. That release closes RGX blocker `PGEN-RGX-0005` by adding named recursion-condition support in conditionals, so `(?(R&name)...)` now parses and transports through `conditional` / `recursion_condition` without changing regex AST schema version `1`.
Tracker note (2026-03-29): regex handoff is now published as downstream maintenance release `1.1.1`. That release fixes four real RGX-reported accepted-tree transport bugs in the generated backend without changing the regex JSON schema version:
- `(?R)` now transports as `subroutine_call` / `subroutine_target` instead of `inline_modifiers`
- `\1` now transports as `backreference` instead of generic `escape`
- `(?(1)a|b)` now preserves separate `yes_branch` / `no_branch` spans
- `ab+` now transports with final-atom quantifier binding
Tracker note (2026-03-29): RGX's re-review of [docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md](docs/contracts/PGEN_REGEX_PARSER_INTEGRATION_CONTRACT.md) now treats regex handoff `1.1.1` as good enough to start downstream integration. The remaining caveats are narrower and no longer blocker-shaped:
- AST JSON is shape-stable but still requires parser-release pinning for detailed semantic rule taxonomy assumptions
- JS/Lua/Rhai code-block support is intentionally narrower than arbitrary valid source acceptance
- `native` / `wasm` tags are now structurally published, but their payload semantics remain downstream-runtime territory
- runtime execution semantics and host-language wrapper parsing remain explicitly out of scope
Tracker interpretation: those remaining regex items are now contract-widening choices, not blockers against beginning downstream integration on the published `1.1.7` surface.

Tracker note (2026-04-05): recorded a no-risk design contract for first-class unlimited lookahead without changing any live-status row. Tracker note (2026-04-06): the corrected last-PGEN CI log then showed that the same `ebnf_frontend_dual_run_diff` lane still has one real repository dependency on the old Perl frontend surface, again without changing any live-status row. The active EBNF frontend direction is still Rust, but this differential-proof lane intentionally retains Perl as a reference oracle and therefore still runs `tools/ebnf_to_json.pl` during bootstrap. The GitHub failure was not a Rust frontend regression; it was a clean-runner dependency bug: `perl/LinkedSpec.pm` compile-loaded `PathSearch`, but `PathSearch.pm` lived only under `fx/perl`, with local shells hiding that through `PERL5LIB`. `perl/LinkedSpec.pm` now appends repo-local `fx/perl` into `@INC` automatically, and the dual-run failure helper now preserves the real bootstrap exit code instead of falsely printing `0`. Clean-environment proofs now pass for both `env -u PERL5LIB perl tools/ebnf_to_json.pl --pretty --quiet grammars/ebnf.ebnf -o ...` and `env -u PERL5LIB make -C rust SHELL=/bin/bash ebnf_frontend_dual_run_diff`. Tracker note (2026-04-06): the published regex downstream contract now also clarifies one architecture/host-surface nuance without changing any live-status row. `parse_session_model=stateless_per_call` in the regex integration documents should be read as a host-API invariant, not as a claim that the generated Rust parser implementation itself is internally stateless. The generated parser remains stateful per parser instance during a call (`position`, memoization, recursion guard, semantic runtime), while downstream consumers should still treat each public parse API call as an independent parse session. This is documentation precision only; it does not widen regex capability or alter the current recommendation that RGX continue its compiler-pass handling for `(?x)` under the present published contract.

This closes the last public-doc mismatch on that nuance; no parser implementation or downstream capability changed in this wave.

Honest fix = constrain the closed-loop stimuli generator's regex-content so a permissive class does not emit the grammar's structural prefix sigil (all-grammars, high blast radius — careful `stimuli_generator.rs` design + cross-parser regression); never loosen `==0`, deliberately not bug-ledger'd), so the preprocessor zero-plausible-gap proof + SV family-status umbrella are still not green pending `.2.3` (and SV-main A3 separately pending `.3`).
